Utah Code Annotated - Title 63N - Economic Opportunity Act
==========================================================

Utah Code Annotated - Title 63N - Chapter 1a - Economic Opportunity Organization
********************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102 Definitions.
---------------------------------------------
As used in this title:Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(1): "Baseline jobs" means the number of full-time employee positions that existed within a business entity in the state before the date on which a project related to the business entity is approved by the office or by the GOEO board.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(2): "Baseline state revenue" means the amount of state tax revenue collected from a business entity or the employees of a business entity during the year before the date on which a project related to the business entity is approved by the office or by the GOEO board.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(3): 63N-1a-201 "Commission" means the Unified Economic Opportunity Commission created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(4): "Economic opportunity agency" includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(4)(a): the Department of Workforce Services;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(4)(b): the Department of Cultural and Community Engagement;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(4)(c): the Department of Commerce;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(4)(d): the Department of Natural Resources;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(4)(e): the Office of Energy Development;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(4)(f): the State Board of Education;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(4)(g): institutions of higher education;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(4)(h): the Utah Multicultural Commission;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(4)(i): the World Trade Center Utah;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(4)(j): local government entities;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(4)(k): associations of governments;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(4)(l): the Utah League of Cities and Towns;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(4)(m): the Utah Association of Counties;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(4)(n): the Economic Development Corporation of Utah;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(4)(o): the Small Business Administration;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(4)(p): chambers of commerce;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(4)(q): industry associations;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(4)(r): small business development centers; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(4)(s): other entities identified by the commission or the executive director.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(5): "Executive director" means the executive director of the office.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(6): "Full-time employee" means an employment position that is filled by an employee who works at least 30 hours per week and:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(6)(a): may include an employment position filled by more than one employee, if each employee who works less than 30 hours per week is provided benefits comparable to a full-time employee; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(6)(b): may not include an employment position that is shifted from one jurisdiction in the state to another jurisdiction in the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(7): 63N-1a-401 "GOEO board" means the Board of Economic Opportunity created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(8): "High paying job" means a newly created full-time employee position where the aggregate average annual gross wage of the employment position, not including health care or other paid or unpaid benefits, is:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(8)(a): at least 110% of the average wage of the county in which the employment position exists; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(8)(b): for an employment position related to a project described in Chapter 2, Part 1, Economic Development Tax Increment Financing, and that is located within the boundary of a county of the third, fourth, fifth, or sixth class, or located within a municipality in a county of the second class and where the municipality has a population of 10,000 or less:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(8)(b)(i): at least 100% of the average wage of the county in which the employment position exists; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(8)(b)(ii): an amount determined by rule made by the office in accordance with Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act, if the office determines the project is in a county experiencing economic distress.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(9): 31A-40-102
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(9)(a): "Incremental job" means a full-time employment position in the state that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(9)(a)(i): did not exist within a business entity in the state before the beginning of a project related to the business entity; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(9)(a)(ii): is created in addition to the number of baseline jobs that existed within a business entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(9)(b): 31A-40-102 "Incremental job" includes a full-time employment position where the employee is hired:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(9)(b)(i): directly by a business entity; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(9)(b)(ii): 31A-40-102 by a professional employer organization, as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(10): "New state revenue" means the state revenue collected from a business entity or a business entity's employees during a calendar year minus the baseline state revenue calculation.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(11): "Office" or "GOEO" means the Governor's Office of Economic Opportunity.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(12): "State revenue" means state tax liability paid by a business entity or a business entity's employees under any combination of the following provisions:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(12)(a): Title 59, Chapter 7, Corporate Franchise and Income Taxes;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(12)(b): Title 59, Chapter 10, Part 1, Determination and Reporting of Tax Liability and Information;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(12)(c): Title 59, Chapter 10, Part 2, Trusts and Estates;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(12)(d): Title 59, Chapter 10, Part 4, Withholding of Tax; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(12)(e): Title 59, Chapter 12, Sales and Use Tax Act.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(13): 63N-1a-103 "State strategic goals" means the strategic goals listed in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(14): 63N-1a-202 "Statewide economic development strategy" means the economic development strategy developed by the commission in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(15): 53B-34-102 "Talent board" means the Talent, Education, and Industry Alignment Board created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-102(16): 63N-1a-202 "Targeted industry" means an industry or group of industries targeted by the commission under Section


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-103 Purpose.
-----------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-103(1): The purpose of the Economic Opportunity Act and the entities established in the act is to catalyze strategic economic opportunities for all residents of the state with a vision of creating economically thriving communities, businesses, and families throughout the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-103(2): The purpose is realized through targeted efforts that demonstrably improve quality of life, measured by the extent to which the efforts accomplish the following strategic goals:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-103(2)(a): catalyzing targeted industry growth;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-103(2)(b): supporting economically thriving communities;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-103(2)(c): empowering students and workers with market-relevant skills;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-103(2)(d): stimulating economic growth in rural and multicultural communities through household level efforts; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-103(2)(e): securing healthy and resilient ecosystems for current and future generations.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-201 Creation of commission.
--------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-201(1): 63N-1a-103 There is created in the office the Unified Economic Opportunity Commission, established to carry out the purpose described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-201(2): 11-58-201; 11-59-201; 63H-1-201 The commission consists of:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-201(2)(a): the following voting members:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-201(2)(a)(i): the governor, who shall serve as the chair of the commission;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-201(2)(a)(ii): the executive director, who shall serve as the vice chair of the commission;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-201(2)(a)(iii): the executive director of the Department of Workforce Services;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-201(2)(a)(iv): the executive director of the Department of Transportation;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-201(2)(a)(v): the executive director of the Department of Natural Resources;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-201(2)(a)(vi): the executive director of the Department of Commerce;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-201(2)(a)(vii): the commissioner of the Department of Agriculture and Food;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-201(2)(a)(viii): the executive director of the Governor's Office of Planning and Budget;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-201(2)(a)(ix): the commissioner of higher education;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-201(2)(a)(x): the state superintendent of public instruction;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-201(2)(a)(xi): the president of the Senate ;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-201(2)(a)(xii): the speaker of the House of Representatives ;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-201(2)(a)(xiii): one individual who is knowledgeable about housing needs in the state, including housing density and land use, appointed by the governor;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-201(2)(a)(xiv): one individual who represents the interests of urban cities, appointed by the Utah League of Cities and Towns; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-201(2)(a)(xv): one individual who represents the interests of rural counties, appointed by the Utah Association of Counties; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-201(2)(b): 11-58-201; 11-59-201; 63H-1-201 the following non-voting members:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-201(2)(b)(i): the chief executive officer of World Trade Center Utah;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-201(2)(b)(ii): the chief executive officer of the Economic Development Corporation of Utah;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-201(2)(b)(iii): a senior advisor to the chair of the commission with expertise in rural affairs of the state, appointed by the chair of the commission; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-201(2)(b)(iv): 11-58-201; 11-59-201; 63H-1-201 the chief executive officer of one of the following entities, appointed by the chair of the commission:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-201(2)(b)(iv)(A): 11-58-201 the Utah Inland Port Authority created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-201(2)(b)(iv)(B): 11-59-201 the Point of the Mountain State Land Authority created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-201(2)(b)(iv)(C): 63H-1-201 the Military Installation Development Authority created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-201(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-201(3)(a): A majority of commission members, not including a vacancy, constitutes a quorum for the purpose of conducting commission business .
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-201(3)(b): The action of a majority of a quorum constitutes the action of the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-201(4): The executive director of the office, or the executive director's designee, is the executive director of the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-201(5): The office shall provide:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-201(5)(a): office space and administrative staff support for the commission; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-201(5)(b): the central leadership and coordination of the commission's efforts in the field of economic development.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-201(6): 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107; 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107; 36-2-2
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-201(6)(a): 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107; 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107 A member may not receive compensation or benefits for the member's service on the commission, but may receive per diem and travel expenses in accordance with:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-201(6)(a)(i): 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107 Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-201(6)(a)(ii): 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107 rules made by the Division of Finance in accordance with Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-201(6)(b): 36-2-2 Compensation and expenses of a commission member who is a legislator are governed by Section


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-202 Commission duties.
---------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-202(1): 73-1-21; 63N-1a-103 The commission shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-202(1)(a): develop, coordinate, and lead a comprehensive statewide economic development strategy that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-202(1)(a)(i): unifies and coordinates economic development efforts in the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-202(1)(a)(ii): includes key performance indicators for long-term progress toward the state strategic goals;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-202(1)(a)(iii): establishes reporting and accountability processes for the key performance indicators; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-202(1)(a)(iv): ensures the success of the statewide economic development strategy is shared among the urban and rural areas of the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-202(1)(b): receive feedback, input, and reports from economic opportunity agencies regarding programs related to the statewide economic development strategy;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-202(1)(c): 73-1-21 develop the statewide economic strategy in view of the state water policy described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-202(1)(d): 63N-1a-103 direct and facilitate changes to or recommend elimination of economic development programs to ensure alignment with the purpose described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-202(1)(e): at least once every five years, identify which industries or groups of industries shall be targeted for economic development in the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-202(1)(f): establish strategies for the recruitment and retention of targeted industries while respecting the different needs of rural and urban areas throughout the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-202(1)(g): establish strategies for supporting entrepreneurship and small business development in the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-202(1)(h): analyze the state's projected long-term population and economic growth and plan for the anticipated impacts of the projected growth in a manner that improves quality of life and is consistent with the statewide economic development strategy and state strategic goals;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-202(1)(i): identify gaps and potential solutions related to improving infrastructure, especially as related to the state's projected long-term population growth;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-202(1)(j): support the development of a prepared workforce that can support targeted industries identified by the commission;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-202(1)(k): coordinate and develop strategies that assist education providers and industry to cooperate in supporting students in developing market relevant skills to meet industry needs;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-202(1)(l): develop strategies and plans to ensure comprehensive economic development efforts are targeted to the unique needs of rural areas of the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-202(1)(m): study the unique needs of multicultural communities throughout the state and develop household-level plans to ensure residents of the state can participate in economic opportunities in the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-202(1)(n): ensure the commission's efforts are, to the extent practicable, data-driven and evidence-based;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-202(1)(o): support an integrated international trade strategy for the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-202(1)(p): facilitate coordination among public, private, and nonprofit economic opportunity agencies; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-202(1)(q): in performing the commission's duties, consider the recommendations of the subcommittees described in Chapter 1b, Commission Subcommittees, the GOEO board, the talent board, and any working groups established under Subsection (2).
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-202(2): The commission may establish working groups as is appropriate to assist and advise the commission on specified topics or issues related to the commission's duties.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-202(3): 63N-1a-306 The commission shall provide a report to the office for inclusion in the office's annual written report described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-202(3)(a): the activity to achieve the statewide economic development strategy;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-202(3)(b): a description of how the commission fulfilled the commission's statutory purposes and duties during the year, including any relevant findings;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-202(3)(c): the key performance indicators included in the statewide economic development strategy, including data showing the extent to which the indicators are being met; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-202(3)(d): any legislative recommendations.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-301 Creation of office -- Responsibilities.
------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-301(1): There is created the Governor's Office of Economic Opportunity.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-301(2): The office is:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-301(2)(a): responsible for implementing the statewide economic development strategy developed by the commission; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-301(2)(b): the industrial and business promotion authority of the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-301(3): 11-41-103; 63N-1a-306 The office shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-301(3)(a): consistent with the statewide economic development strategy, coordinate and align into a single effort the activities of the economic opportunity agencies in the field of economic development;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-301(3)(b): provide support and direction to economic opportunity agencies in establishing goals, metrics, and activities that align with the statewide economic development strategy;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-301(3)(c): administer and coordinate state and federal economic development grant programs;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-301(3)(d): promote and encourage the economic, commercial, financial, industrial, agricultural, and civic welfare of the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-301(3)(e): promote and encourage the employment of workers in the state and the purchase of goods and services produced in the state by local businesses;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-301(3)(f): 11-41-103 act to create, develop, attract, and retain business, industry, and commerce in the state:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-301(3)(f)(i): in accordance with the statewide economic development plan and commission directives; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-301(3)(f)(ii): 11-41-103 subject to the restrictions in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-301(3)(g): act to enhance the state's economy;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-301(3)(h): act to assist strategic industries that are likely to drive future economic growth;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-301(3)(i): assist communities in the state in developing economic development capacity and coordination with other communities;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-301(3)(j): identify areas of education and workforce development in the state that can be improved to support economic and business development;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-301(3)(k): consistent with direction from the commission, develop core strategic priorities for the office, which may include:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-301(3)(k)(i): enhancing statewide access to entrepreneurship opportunities and small business support;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-301(3)(k)(ii): focusing industry recruitment and expansion of targeted industries;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-301(3)(k)(iii): ensuring that in awarding competitive economic development incentives the office accurately measures the benefits and costs of the incentives; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-301(3)(k)(iv): assisting communities with technical support to aid those communities in improving economic development opportunities;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-301(3)(l): 63N-1a-306 submit an annual written report as described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-301(3)(m): perform other duties as provided by the Legislature.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-301(4): To perform the office's duties under this title, the office may:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-301(4)(a): enter into a contract or agreement with, or make a grant to, a public or private entity, including a municipality, if the contract or agreement is not in violation of state statute or other applicable law;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-301(4)(b): except as provided in Subsection (4)(c), receive and expend funds from a public or private source for any lawful purpose that is in the state's best interest; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-301(4)(c): solicit and accept a contribution of money, services, or facilities from a public or private donor, but may not use the contribution for publicizing the exclusive interest of the donor.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-301(5): Money received under Subsection (4)(c) shall be deposited into the General Fund as dedicated credits of the office.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-301(6): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-301(6)(a): The office shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-301(6)(a)(i): obtain the advice of the GOEO board before implementing a change to a policy, priority, or objective under which the office operates; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-301(6)(a)(ii): provide periodic updates to the commission regarding the office's efforts under Subsections (3)(a) and (b).
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-301(6)(b): Subsection (6)(a)(i) does not apply to the routine administration by the office of money or services related to the assistance, retention, or recruitment of business, industry, or commerce in the state.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-302 Executive director of office -- Appointment -- Removal -- Compensation.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-302(1): The office shall be administered, organized, and managed by an executive director appointed by the governor, with the advice and consent of the Senate.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-302(2): The executive director serves at the pleasure of the governor.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-302(3): Title 67, Chapter 22, State Officer Compensation The salary of the executive director shall be established by the governor within the salary range fixed by the Legislature in


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-303 Powers and duties of executive director.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-303(1): Unless otherwise expressly provided by statute, the executive director may organize the office in any appropriate manner, including the appointment of deputy directors of the office.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-303(2): The executive director may consolidate personnel and service functions for efficiency and economy in the office.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-303(3): Title 63J, Chapter 5, Federal Funds Procedures Act The executive director, with the approval of the governor:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-303(3)(a): Title 63J, Chapter 5, Federal Funds Procedures Act may, by following the procedures and requirements of
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-303(3)(b): may enter into a lawful contract or agreement with another state, a chamber of commerce organization, a service club, or a private entity; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-303(3)(c): shall annually prepare and submit to the governor a budget of the office's financial requirements.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-303(4): With the governor's approval, if a federal program requires the expenditure of state funds as a condition for the state to participate in a fund, property, or service, the executive director may expend necessary funds from money provided by the Legislature for the use of the office.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-303(5): 63N-1a-306(2)(b) The executive director shall coordinate with the executive directors of the Department of Workforce Services and the Governor's Office of Planning and Budget to review data and metrics to be reported to the Legislature as described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-303(6): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act Unless otherwise provided in this title, the executive director may make rules in accordance with


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-304 Executive director and the Public Service Commission.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-304(1): The executive director or the executive director's designee shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-304(1)(a): become generally informed of significant rate cases and policy proceedings before the Public Service Commission; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-304(1)(b): monitor and study the potential economic development impact of these proceedings.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-304(2): In the discretion of the executive director or the executive director's designee, the office may appear in a proceeding before the Public Service Commission to testify, advise, or present argument regarding the economic development impact of a matter that is the subject of the proceeding.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-305 Incentive review process.
----------------------------------------------------------
The Legislature intends that the office will develop an incentives review process under the direction of the speaker of the House and the president of the Senate.

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-306 Annual report -- Content -- Format.
--------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-306(1): The office shall prepare and submit to the governor and the Legislature, by October 1 of each year, an annual written report of the operations, activities, programs, and services of the office, including the divisions, sections, boards, commissions, councils, and committees established under this title, for the preceding fiscal year.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-306(2): (2)(b); (c) For each operation, activity, program, or service provided by the office, the annual report shall include:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-306(2)(a): a description of the operation, activity, program, or service;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-306(2)(b): data and metrics:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-306(2)(b)(i): selected and used by the office to measure progress, performance, effectiveness, and scope of the operation, activity, program, or service, including summary data; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-306(2)(b)(ii): that are consistent and comparable for each state operation, activity, program, or service that primarily involves employment training or placement as determined by the executive directors of the office, the Department of Workforce Services, and the Governor's Office of Planning and Budget;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-306(2)(c): budget data, including the amount and source of funding, expenses, and allocation of full-time employees for the operation, activity, program, or service;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-306(2)(d): (2)(b); (c) historical data from previous years for comparison with data reported under Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-306(2)(e): goals, challenges, and achievements related to the operation, activity, program, or service;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-306(2)(f): relevant federal and state statutory references and requirements;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-306(2)(g): contact information of officials knowledgeable and responsible for each operation, activity, program, or service; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-306(2)(h): other information determined by the office that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-306(2)(h)(i): may be needed, useful, or of historical significance; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-306(2)(h)(ii): promotes accountability and transparency for each operation, activity, program, or service with the public and elected officials.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-306(3): The annual report shall be designed to provide clear, accurate, and accessible information to the public, the governor, and the Legislature.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-306(4): 68-3-14; (2)(b) The office shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-306(4)(a): 68-3-14 submit the annual report in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-306(4)(b): make the annual report, and previous annual reports, accessible to the public by placing a link to the reports on the office's website; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-306(4)(c): (2)(b) provide the data and metrics described in Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-307 Restrictions on direct award grants.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-307(1): 63G-6b-101 As used in this section, "direct award grant" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-307(2): Title 63G, Chapter 6b, State Grants In addition to the requirements of
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-307(3): If an item of appropriation to the office for a direct award grant does not include any standards or criteria for distributing the grant funds, the funds shall lapse to the source fund at the end of the fiscal year, regardless of whether those funds are designated by law as nonlapsing.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-401 Creation of Board of Economic Opportunity.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-401(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-401(1)(a): There is created within the office the Board of Economic Opportunity, consisting of nine members appointed by the chair of the commission, in consultation with the executive director, to four-year terms of office with the advice and consent of the Senate in accordance with Title 63G, Chapter 24, Part 2, Vacancies.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-401(1)(b): The nine members described in Subsection (1)(a) shall include:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-401(1)(b)(i): one member associated with the state's rural communities;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-401(1)(b)(ii): one member associated with direct entrepreneurship in the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-401(1)(b)(iii): one member associated with higher education in the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-401(1)(b)(iv): five members, other than the members described in Subsections (1)(b)(i) through (iii), that are associated with a targeted industry; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-401(1)(b)(v): one at-large member.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-401(1)(c): Notwithstanding the requirements of Subsection (1)(a), the chair of the commission shall, at the time of appointment or reappointment, adjust the length of terms to ensure that the terms of board members are staggered so that approximately half of the board is appointed every two years.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-401(1)(d): The members may not serve more than two full consecutive terms except when the chair of the commission determines that an additional term is in the best interest of the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-401(2): When a vacancy occurs in the membership for any reason, the replacement shall be appointed for the unexpired term in accordance with Title 63G, Chapter 24, Part 2, Vacancies.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-401(3): A majority of board members, not including a vacancy, constitutes a quorum for conducting board business and exercising board power.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-401(4): The chair of the commission shall select one board member as the board's chair and one member as the board's vice chair.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-401(5): 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107; 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107 A member may not receive compensation or benefits for the member's service, but may receive per diem and travel expenses in accordance with:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-401(5)(a): 63A-3-106 Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-401(5)(b): 63A-3-107 Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-401(5)(c): 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107 rules made by the Division of Finance under Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-401(6): A member shall comply with the conflict of interest provisions described in Title 63G, Chapter 24, Part 3, Conflicts of Interest.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-402 Board of Economic Opportunity duties and powers.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-402(1): The GOEO board shall advise and assist the office to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-402(1)(a): promote and encourage the economic, commercial, financial, industrial, agricultural, and civic welfare of the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-402(1)(b): promote and encourage the development, attraction, expansion, and retention of businesses, industries, and commerce in the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-402(1)(c): support the efforts of local government and regional nonprofit economic development organizations to encourage expansion or retention of businesses, industries, and commerce in the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-402(1)(d): act to enhance the state's economy;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-402(1)(e): develop policies, priorities, and objectives regarding the assistance, retention, or recruitment of business, industries, and commerce in the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-402(1)(f): administer programs for the assistance, retention, or recruitment of businesses, industries, and commerce in the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-402(1)(g): ensure that economic development programs are available to all areas of the state in accordance with federal and state law;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-402(1)(h): identify local, regional, and statewide rural economic development and planning priorities;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-402(1)(i): understand, through study and input, issues relating to local, regional, and statewide rural economic development, including challenges, opportunities, best practices, policy, planning, and collaboration; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-402(1)(j): maintain ethical and conflict of interest standards consistent with those imposed on a public officer under Title 67, Chapter 16, Utah Public Officers' and Employees' Ethics Act.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1a-402(2): In accordance with Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act, the GOEO board may, in consultation with the executive director, make rules for the conduct of the GOEO board's business.

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-402 Women in the Economy Subcommittee created.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-402(1): There is created a subcommittee of the commission called the Women in the Economy Subcommittee.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-402(2): The subcommittee shall consist of 15 members as follows:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-402(2)(a): one senator appointed by the president of the Senate;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-402(2)(b): one senator appointed by the minority leader of the Senate;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-402(2)(c): one representative appointed by the speaker of the House of Representatives;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-402(2)(d): one representative appointed by the minority leader of the House of Representatives;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-402(2)(e): the executive director of the department, or the executive director's designee; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-402(2)(f): 10 members appointed by the governor as follows:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-402(2)(f)(i): two individuals who represent businesses in the state that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-402(2)(f)(i)(A): have fewer than 50 employees; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-402(2)(f)(i)(B): have demonstrated a commitment to women in the economy;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-402(2)(f)(ii): two individuals who represent businesses in the state that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-402(2)(f)(ii)(A): have 50 or more employees, but fewer than 500 employees; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-402(2)(f)(ii)(B): have demonstrated a commitment to women in the economy;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-402(2)(f)(iii): two individuals who represent businesses in the state that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-402(2)(f)(iii)(A): have 500 or more employees; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-402(2)(f)(iii)(B): have demonstrated a commitment to women in the economy;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-402(2)(f)(iv): an individual who has experience in economic and demographic work;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-402(2)(f)(v): one individual from a nonprofit organization that focuses on women's advocacy;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-402(2)(f)(vi): one individual with managerial experience with organized labor; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-402(2)(f)(vii): one individual who serves as an officer, employee, or appointee of a local government, nominated by the Utah League of Cities and Towns.

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-403 Purpose -- Powers and duties of the subcommittee.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-403(1): The subcommittee's purpose is to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-403(1)(a): increase public and government understanding of the current and future impact and needs of the state's women in the economy and how those needs may be most effectively and efficiently met;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-403(1)(b): identify and recommend implementation of specific policies, procedures, and programs to respond to the rights, needs, and impact of women in the economy; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-403(1)(c): facilitate coordination of the functions of public and private entities concerned with women in the economy.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-403(2): The subcommittee shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-403(2)(a): facilitate the communication and coordination of public and private entities that provide services to women or protect the rights of women;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-403(2)(b): study, evaluate, and report on the status and effectiveness of policies, procedures, and programs that provide services to women or protect the rights of women;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-403(2)(c): study and evaluate the policies, procedures, and programs implemented by other states that address the needs of women in the economy or protect the rights of women;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-403(2)(d): facilitate and conduct the research and study of issues related to women in the economy;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-403(2)(e): provide a forum for public comment on issues related to women in the economy;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-403(2)(f): provide public information on women in the economy and the services available to women; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-403(2)(g): encourage state and local governments to analyze, plan, and prepare for the impact of women in the economy on services and operations.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-403(3): To accomplish the subcommittee's duties, the subcommittee may:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-403(3)(a): request and receive from a state or local government agency or institution summary information relating to women in the economy, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-403(3)(a)(i): reports;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-403(3)(a)(ii): audits;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-403(3)(a)(iii): projections; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-403(3)(a)(iv): statistics;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-403(3)(b): in coordination with the office, apply for and accept grants or donations for uses consistent with the duties of the subcommittee from public or private sources; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-403(3)(c): appoint one or more working groups to advise and assist the subcommittee.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-403(4): (3)(b) Money received by the office under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-403(4)(a): accounted for and expended in compliance with the requirements of federal and state law; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-403(4)(b): continuously available to the subcommittee to carry out the subcommittee's duties.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-403(5): (3)(c); 63N-1b-402; (3)(c)
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-403(5)(a): (3)(c); 63N-1b-402 A member of a working group described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-403(5)(a)(i): shall be appointed by the subcommittee;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-403(5)(a)(ii): may be:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-403(5)(a)(ii)(A): a member of the subcommittee; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-403(5)(a)(ii)(B): an individual from the private or public sector; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-403(5)(a)(iii): 63N-1b-402 notwithstanding Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-403(5)(b): (3)(c) A working group described in Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-404 Annual report.
-----------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-404(1): 63N-1a-202 The subcommittee shall annually prepare a report for inclusion in the commission's report to the office under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-404(2): The report described in Subsection (1) shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-404(2)(a): describe how the subcommittee fulfilled the subcommittee's statutory purposes and duties during the year; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-1b-404(2)(b): contain recommendations on how the state should act to address issues relating to women in the economy.


Utah Code Annotated - Title 63N - Chapter 2 - Tax Credit Incentives for Economic Development
********************************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-101 Title.
--------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-101(1): This chapter is known as "Tax Credit Incentives for Economic Development."
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-101(2): This part is known as "Economic Development Tax Increment Financing."


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-102 Purpose.
----------------------------------------
This part is enacted to:Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-102(1): foster and develop targeted industries in the state, to stimulate community-focused economic growth, and to diversify and catalyze the state's economy;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-102(2): create high paying employment opportunities in the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-102(3): provide tax credits to attract new commercial projects and new jobs in economic development zones in the state; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-102(4): provide a cooperative and unified working relationship between state and local economic development efforts.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-103 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-103(1): 59-7-614.2; 59-10-1107; 63N-2-104.3
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-103(1)(a): 59-7-614.2; 59-10-1107 "Business entity" means a person that enters into a written agreement with the office to initiate a new commercial project in Utah that will qualify the person to receive a tax credit under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-103(1)(b): 63N-2-104.3 With respect to a tax credit authorized by the office in accordance with Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-103(2): "Commercial or industrial zone" means an area zoned agricultural, commercial, industrial, manufacturing, business park, research park, or other appropriate business related use in a general plan that contemplates future growth.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-103(3): 63N-2-104 "Development zone" means an economic development zone created under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-103(4): "Local government entity" means a county, city, or town.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-103(5): "New commercial project" means an economic development opportunity that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-103(5)(a): involves a targeted industry;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-103(5)(b): is located within:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-103(5)(b)(i): a county of the third, fourth, fifth, or sixth class; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-103(5)(b)(ii): a municipality that has a population of 10,000 or less and the municipality is located within a county of the second class; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-103(5)(c): involves an economic development opportunity that the commission determines to be eligible for a tax credit under this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-103(6): "Remote work opportunity" means a new commercial project that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-103(6)(a): does not require a physical office in the state where employees associated with the new commercial project are required to work; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-103(6)(b): requires employees associated with the new commercial project to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-103(6)(b)(i): work remotely from a location within the state; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-103(6)(b)(ii): maintain residency in the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-103(7): "Significant capital investment" means an investment in capital or fixed assets, which may include real property, personal property, and other fixtures related to a new commercial project that represents an expansion of existing operations in the state or that increases the business entity's existing workforce in the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-103(8): 59-7-614.2; 59-10-1107 "Tax credit" means an economic development tax credit created by Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-103(9): "Tax credit amount" means the amount the office lists as a tax credit on a tax credit certificate for a taxable year.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-103(10): "Tax credit certificate" means a certificate issued by the office that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-103(10)(a): lists the name of the business entity to which the office authorizes a tax credit;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-103(10)(b): lists the business entity's taxpayer identification number;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-103(10)(c): lists the amount of tax credit that the office authorizes the business entity for the taxable year; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-103(10)(d): may include other information as determined by the office.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-103(11): 63N-2-104.2 "Written agreement" means a written agreement entered into between the office and a business entity under Section


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104 Creation of economic development zones -- Tax credits -- Assignment of tax credit.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104(1): (1)(b) The office may create an economic development zone in the state if the following requirements are satisfied:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104(1)(a): the area is located within a commercial or industrial zone;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104(1)(b): the local government entity having jurisdiction over the area supports the creation of the development zone; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104(1)(c): (1)(b) the local government entity described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104(2): A local government entity may, for the purpose of incentivizing new commercial projects within the local government entity's boundaries, create an economic development zone if the following requirements are satisfied:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104(2)(a): the area is located:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104(2)(a)(i): within a commercial or industrial zone; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104(2)(a)(ii): within the geographic boundaries of the local government entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104(2)(b): the local government entity adopts a long-term plan that addresses the following planning elements within the area:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104(2)(b)(i): transportation and infrastructure;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104(2)(b)(ii): workforce development; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104(2)(b)(iii): housing needs; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104(2)(c): the office approves the local government entity's request to create the development zone.

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104.2(1)(e): requires the business entity to submit to audits for verification of any tax credit claimed; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104.2(1)(f): 63N-2-105 requires the business entity, in order to claim a tax credit, to meet the requirements of Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104.2(2): 63N-2-104 In establishing the terms of a written agreement, including the duration and amount of tax credit that the business entity may be authorized to receive, the office shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104.2(2)(a): authorize the tax credit in a manner that provides the most effective incentive for the new commercial project;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104.2(2)(b): 63N-2-104 consider the following factors:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104.2(2)(b)(i): whether the new commercial project provides vital or specialized support to supply chains;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104.2(2)(b)(ii): whether the new commercial project provides an innovative product, technology, or service;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104.2(2)(b)(iii): the number and wages of new incremental jobs associated with the new commercial project;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104.2(2)(b)(iv): the amount of financial support provided by local government entities for the new commercial project;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104.2(2)(b)(v): the amount of capital expenditures associated with the new commercial project;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104.2(2)(b)(vi): whether the new commercial project returns jobs transferred overseas;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104.2(2)(b)(vii): the rate of unemployment in the county in which the new commercial project is located;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104.2(2)(b)(viii): whether the new commercial project creates a remote work opportunity;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104.2(2)(b)(ix): 63N-2-104 whether the new commercial project is located in a development zone created by a local government entity as described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104.2(2)(b)(x): whether the business entity commits to hiring Utah workers for the new commercial project;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104.2(2)(b)(xi): whether the business entity adopts a corporate citizenry plan or supports initiatives in the state that advance education, gender equality, diversity and inclusion, work-life balance, environmental or social good, or other similar causes;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104.2(2)(b)(xii): whether the business entity's headquarters are located within the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104.2(2)(b)(xiii): the likelihood of other business entities relocating to another state as a result of the new commercial project;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104.2(2)(b)(xiv): the necessity of the tax credit for the business entity's expansion in the state or relocation from another state;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104.2(2)(b)(xv): whether the proposed new commercial project might reasonably be expected to occur in the foreseeable future without the tax credit; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104.2(2)(b)(xvi): the location and impact of the new commercial project on existing and planned transportation facilities, existing and planned housing, including affordable housing, and public infrastructure; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104.2(2)(c): consult with the GOEO board.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104.2(3): 63N-2-104 In determining the amount of tax credit that a business entity may be authorized to receive under a written agreement, the office may:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104.2(3)(a): 63N-2-104 authorize a higher or optimized amount of tax credit for a new commercial project located within a development zone created by a local government entity as described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104.2(3)(b): establish by rule made in accordance with Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act, a process by which the office closely approximates the amount of taxes the business entity paid under Title 59, Chapter 12, Sales and Use Tax Act, for a capital project.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104.2(4): If the office identifies any of the following events after entering into a written agreement with a business entity, the office and the business entity shall amend, or the office may terminate, the written agreement:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104.2(4)(a): a change in the business entity's organization resulting from a merger with or acquisition of another entity located in the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104.2(4)(b): a material increase in the business entity's retail operations that results in new state revenue not subject to the incentive; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104.2(4)(c): an increase in the business entity's operations that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104.2(4)(c)(i): is outside the scope of the written agreement or outside the boundaries of a development zone; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104.2(4)(c)(ii): results in new state revenue not subject to the incentive.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104.3 Limitations on tax credit amount.
-------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104.3(1): (2)(a) Except as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104.3(1)(a): 50% of the new state revenues from the new commercial project in any given year;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104.3(1)(b): 30% of the new state revenues from the new commercial project over a period of up to 20 years; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104.3(1)(c): 35% of the new state revenues from the new commercial project over a period of up to 20 years, if:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104.3(1)(c)(i): the new commercial project brings 2,500 or more new incremental jobs to the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104.3(1)(c)(ii): the amount of capital expenditures associated with the new commercial project is $1,000,000,000 or more; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104.3(1)(c)(iii): the commission approves the tax credit.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104.3(2): If the office authorizes a tax credit for a new commercial project located within the boundary of:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104.3(2)(a): a municipality with a population of 10,000 or less located within a county of the second class and that is experiencing economic hardship as determined by the office, the office may authorize a tax credit of up to 50% of new state revenues from the new commercial project over a period of up to 20 years;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104.3(2)(b): a county of the third class, the office may authorize a tax credit of up to 50% of new state revenues from the new commercial project over a period of up to 20 years; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-104.3(2)(c): a county of the fourth, fifth, or sixth class, the office may authorize a tax credit of 50% of new state revenues from the new commercial project over a period of up to 20 years.

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-201 Title.
--------------------------------------
This part is known as the "Enterprise Zone Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-203 Powers of the office.
-----------------------------------------------------
The office shall:Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-203(1): monitor the implementation and operation of this part and conduct a continuing evaluation of the progress made in the enterprise zones;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-203(2): evaluate an application for designation as an enterprise zone from a county applicant or a municipal applicant and determine if the applicant qualifies for that designation;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-203(3): provide technical assistance to county applicants and municipal applicants in developing applications for designation as enterprise zones;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-203(4): assist county applicants and municipal applicants designated as enterprise zones in obtaining assistance from the federal government and agencies of the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-203(5): assist a qualified business entity in obtaining the benefits of an incentive or inducement program authorized by this part; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-203(6): 63N-1a-306 as part of the annual written report described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-203(6)(a): based on data from the State Tax Commission, the total amount of tax credits claimed under this part;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-203(6)(b): the total amount awarded in tax credits for each development zone;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-203(6)(c): the number of new full-time employee positions reported to obtain tax credits in each development zone;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-203(6)(d): the amount of tax credits awarded for rehabilitating a building in each development zone;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-203(6)(e): the amount of tax credits awarded for investing in a plant, equipment, or other depreciable property in each development zone; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-203(6)(f): recommendations regarding the effectiveness of the program and any suggestions for legislation.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-204 Criteria for designation of enterprise zones -- Application.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-204(1): A county applicant seeking designation as an enterprise zone shall file an application with the office that, in addition to complying with the other requirements of this part:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-204(1)(a): verifies that the county has a population of not more than 70,000; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-204(1)(b): provides clear evidence of the need for development in the county.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-204(2): A municipal applicant seeking designation as an enterprise zone shall file an application with the office that, in addition to complying with other requirements of this part:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-204(2)(a): verifies that the municipality has a population that does not exceed 20,000;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-204(2)(b): verifies that the municipality is within a county that has a population of not more than 70,000; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-204(2)(c): provides clear evidence of the need for development in the municipality.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-204(3): (1); (2); 63N-2-205 An application filed under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-204(3)(a): 63N-2-205 a plan developed by the county applicant or municipal applicant that identifies local contributions meeting the requirements of Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-204(3)(b): the county applicant or municipal applicant has a development plan that outlines:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-204(3)(b)(i): the types of investment and development within the zone that the county applicant or municipal applicant expects to take place if the incentives specified in this part are provided;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-204(3)(b)(ii): the specific investment or development reasonably expected to take place;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-204(3)(b)(iii): any commitments obtained from businesses;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-204(3)(b)(iv): the projected number of jobs that will be created and the anticipated wage level of those jobs;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-204(3)(b)(v): any proposed emphasis on the type of jobs created, including any affirmative action plans; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-204(3)(b)(vi): a copy of the county applicant's or municipal applicant's economic development plan to demonstrate coordination between the zone and overall county or municipal goals;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-204(3)(c): the county applicant's or municipal applicant's proposed means of assessing the effectiveness of the development plan or other programs within the zone once they have been implemented within the zone;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-204(3)(d): any additional information required by the office; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-204(3)(e): any additional information the county applicant or municipal applicant considers relevant to its designation as an enterprise zone.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-204(4): On or after January 1, 2021, no new enterprise zones shall be designated.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-205 Qualifying local contributions.
---------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-205(1): An area may be designated as an enterprise zone only if the county applicant or municipal applicant agrees to make a qualifying local contribution.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-205(2): The qualifying local contribution may vary depending on available resources, and may include such elements as:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-205(2)(a): simplified procedures for obtaining permits;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-205(2)(b): dedication of available government grants;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-205(2)(c): dedication of training funds;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-205(2)(d): waiver of business license fees;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-205(2)(e): infrastructure improvements;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-205(2)(f): private contributions;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-205(2)(g): utility rate concessions;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-205(2)(h): small business incubator programs; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-205(2)(i): management assistance programs.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-206 Eligibility review.
---------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-206(1): 63N-2-204 The office shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-206(1)(a): 63N-2-204 review and evaluate the applications submitted under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-206(1)(b): determine whether each county applicant or municipal applicant is eligible for designation as an enterprise zone.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-206(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-206(2)(a): The office shall designate enterprise zones.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-206(2)(b): The office shall consider and evaluate an application using the following criteria:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-206(2)(b)(i): the pervasiveness of poverty, unemployment, and general distress in the proposed zone;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-206(2)(b)(ii): the extent of chronic abandonment, deterioration, or reduction in value of commercial, industrial, or residential structures in the proposed zone, and the extent of property tax arrearages in the proposed zone;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-206(2)(b)(iii): the potential for new investment and economic development in the proposed zone;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-206(2)(b)(iv): the county applicant's or municipal applicant's proposed use of other state and federal development funds or programs to increase the probability of new investment and development occurring;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-206(2)(b)(v): the extent to which the projected development in the zone will provide employment to residents of the county and particularly individuals who are unemployed or who are economically disadvantaged;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-206(2)(b)(vi): the degree to which the county applicant's or municipal applicant's application promotes innovative solutions to economic development problems and demonstrates local initiative; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-206(2)(b)(vii): other relevant factors that the office specifies in its recommendation.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-207 Quarterly consideration.
--------------------------------------------------------
The office shall consider designating enterprise zones quarterly.

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-208 Duration of designation.
--------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-208(1): Each enterprise zone has a duration of five years.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-208(2): On or after January 1, 2021, neither a municipality nor a county may reapply for an enterprise zone designation for an enterprise zone that has reached the end of the enterprise zone's five-year duration.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-209 Contingent designations.
--------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-209(1): The office may accept applications for, and may at any time grant, a contingent designation of any county as an enterprise zone for purposes of seeking a designation of the county as a federally designated zone.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-209(2): This designation does not entitle a business operating in that county to the tax incentives under this part.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-210 Revocation of designations.
-----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-210(1): The office may revoke the designation of an enterprise zone if no businesses utilize the tax incentives during a calendar year.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-210(2): Prior to that action, the office shall conduct a public hearing to determine reasons for inactivity and explore possible alternative actions.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-211 Disqualifying transfers.
--------------------------------------------------------
Except in a county of the first or second class, tax incentives provided by this part are not available to a business entity that closes or permanently curtails operations in another part of the state in connection with a transfer of any part of its business operations to an enterprise zone, if the closure or permanent curtailment is reasonably expected to diminish employment in that part of the state.

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-214 Annual report.
----------------------------------------------
Each county applicant or municipal applicant designated as an enterprise zone shall annually report to the office regarding the economic activity that has occurred in the zone following the designation.

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-303 Duties of the office.
-----------------------------------------------------
The office shall:Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-303(1): monitor the implementation and operation of this part and conduct a continuing evaluation of the effectiveness of the targeted business income tax credit in bringing significant new employment and significant new capital development to rural communities;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-303(2): determine a business entity's eligibility for a targeted business income tax credit award;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-303(3): ensure that tax credits are only awarded under this part to a business applicant that has satisfied performance benchmarks as determined by the office;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-303(4): ensure that the amount of targeted business income tax credit awarded to a business applicant through a targeted business income tax credit eligibility certificate is no more than $100,000 for the business applicant's taxable year;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-303(5): ensure that the aggregate amount of targeted business income tax credits awarded to business applicants through targeted business income tax credit eligibility certificates is no more than $300,000 for each fiscal year;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-303(6): 63N-1a-306 as part of the annual written report described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-303(6)(a): the identity of each business applicant that was provided a targeted business income tax credit eligibility certificate by the office during the year of the annual report; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-303(6)(b): the total amount awarded in targeted business income tax credit for each development zone; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-303(7): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-303(7)(a): the determination of what constitutes:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-303(7)(a)(i): significant new employment;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-303(7)(a)(ii): significant new capital development; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-303(7)(a)(iii): a community investment project;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-303(7)(b): the form and content of an application for a targeted business income tax credit eligibility certificate under this part;

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-303(7)(d): administration of targeted business income tax credit awards and the issuing of targeted business income tax credit eligibility certificates, including relevant timelines and deadlines.

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-501 Title.

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-502(8): "Construction revenue" means revenue generated from state taxes and local taxes imposed on transactions occurring during the eligibility period as a result of the construction of the hotel property, including purchases made by a qualified hotel owner and its subcontractors.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-502(9): "Convention incentive" means an incentive for the development of a qualified hotel, in the form of payment from the incentive fund as provided in this part, as authorized in an agreement.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-502(10): (10)(a) "Eligibility period" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-502(10)(a): the period that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-502(10)(a)(i): begins the date construction of a qualified hotel begins; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-502(10)(a)(ii): ends:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-502(10)(a)(ii)(A): for purposes of the state portion, 20 years after the date of initial occupancy of that qualified hotel; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-502(10)(a)(ii)(B): for purposes of the local portion and incremental property tax revenue, 25 years after the date of initial occupancy of that hotel; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-502(10)(b): (10)(a) as provided in an agreement between the office and a qualified hotel owner or host local government, a period that:

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-502(10)(b)(ii): (10)(a) is shorter than the period described in Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-502(11)(b): signed by the county executive; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-502(11)(c): expressing the county's endorsement of a developer of a qualified hotel as meeting all the county's criteria for receiving the county's endorsement.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-502(12): "Host agency" means the community reinvestment agency of the host local government.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-502(13): "Host local government" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-502(13)(a): a county that enters into an agreement with the office for the construction of a qualified hotel within the unincorporated area of the county; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-502(13)(b): a city or town that enters into an agreement with the office for the construction of a qualified hotel within the boundary of the city or town.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-502(14): "Hotel property" means a qualified hotel and any property that is included in the same development as the qualified hotel, including convention, exhibit, and meeting space, retail shops, restaurants, parking, and other ancillary facilities and amenities.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-502(15): 63N-2-503.5 "Incentive fund" means the Convention Incentive Fund created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-502(16): "Incremental property tax revenue" means the amount of property tax revenue generated from hotel property that equals the difference between:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-502(16)(a): the amount of property tax revenue generated in any tax year by all taxing entities from hotel property, using the current assessed value of the hotel property; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-502(16)(b): the amount of property tax revenue that would be generated that tax year by all taxing entities from hotel property, using the hotel property's base taxable value.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-502(17): "Local portion" means the portion of new tax revenue that is generated by local taxes.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-502(18): 59-12-204; 59-12-301; 59-12-352; 59-12-353; 59-12-603(1)(a); 59-12-1102 "Local taxes" means a tax imposed under:

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-504 Independent review committee.
-------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-504(1): 63N-2-509 In accordance with rules adopted by the office under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-504(2): The review committee shall consist of:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-504(2)(a): one member appointed by the executive director to represent the office;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-504(2)(b): two members appointed by the mayor or chief executive of the county in which the qualified hotel is located or proposed to be located;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-504(2)(c): two members appointed by:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-504(2)(c)(i): the mayor of the municipality in which the qualified hotel is located or proposed to be located, if the qualified hotel is located or proposed to be located within the boundary of a municipality; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-504(2)(c)(ii): the mayor or chief executive of the county in which the qualified hotel is located or proposed to be located, in addition to the two members appointed under Subsection (2)(b), if the qualified hotel is located or proposed to be located outside the boundary of a municipality;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-504(2)(d): an individual representing the hotel industry, appointed by the Utah Hotel and Lodging Association;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-504(2)(e): an individual representing the commercial development and construction industry, appointed by the president or chief executive officer of the local chamber of commerce;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-504(2)(f): an individual representing the convention and meeting planners industry, appointed by the president or chief executive officer of the local convention and visitors bureau; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-504(2)(g): one member appointed by the GOEO board.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-504(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-504(3)(a): A member serves an indeterminate term and may be removed from the review committee by the appointing authority at any time.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-504(3)(b): A vacancy may be filled in the same manner as an appointment under Subsection (2).
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-504(4): A member of the review committee may not be paid for serving on the review committee and may not receive per diem or expense reimbursement.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-504(5): The office shall provide any necessary staff support to the review committee.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-505 Submission of written claim for convention incentive -- Disclosure of tax returns and other information -- Determination of claim.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-505(1): The office may not pay any money from the incentive fund to a qualified hotel owner or host local government unless:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-505(1)(a): the qualified hotel owner or host local government submits a claim and other required documentation, as provided in this section; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-505(1)(b): the office approves and certifies the claim, as provided in this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-505(2): 59-12-211; 59-12-211.1; 59-12-212; 59-12-213; 59-12-214; 59-12-215; 59-1-403; 59-1-403; 59-1-403; 59-1-403 A qualified hotel owner or host local government that desires to qualify for a convention incentive shall submit to the office:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-505(2)(a): a written claim for a convention incentive;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-505(2)(b): 59-12-211; 59-12-211.1; 59-12-212; 59-12-213; 59-12-214; 59-12-215; 59-1-403; 59-1-403; 59-1-403

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-803 Tax credits issued by office.
-------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-803(1): The office may issue tax credit certificates under this part only to the extent that the Legislature, by statute, expressly authorizes the office to issue the tax credit certificates under this part for a fiscal year.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-803(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-803(2)(a): For fiscal year 2011-12 only, the office may issue a total of $1,300,000 in tax credit certificates in accordance with this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-803(2)(b): For fiscal year 2016-17 only, the office may issue a total of $150,000 in tax credit certificates in accordance with this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-803(2)(c): For fiscal year 2017-18 only, the office may issue a total of $150,000 in tax credit certificates in accordance with this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-803(3): If the total amount of tax credit certificates the office issues in a fiscal year is less than the amount of tax credit certificates the office may issue under this part in a fiscal year, the office may issue the remaining amount of tax credit certificates in a fiscal year after the fiscal year for which there is a remaining amount of tax credit certificates.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-804 Person may not claim or pass through a tax credit without tax credit certificate.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
A person may not claim or pass through a tax credit unless the person has received a tax credit certificate from the office for the taxable year for which the person claims or passes through the tax credit.

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-808(1)(b)(ii): require the tax credit certificate recipient to retain records supporting a claim for a tax credit for at least four years after the tax credit certificate recipient claims a tax credit under this part; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-808(1)(b)(iii): require the tax credit certificate recipient to submit to audits for verification of the tax credit claimed, including audits by the office and by the State Tax Commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-808(2): 59-1-403

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-808(2)(b): 59-1-403 The agreement described in Subsection (2)(a):
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-808(2)(b)(i): 59-1-403 shall provide the office with a document that expressly and directly authorizes the State Tax Commission to disclose to the office the life science establishment's tax returns and other information that would otherwise be subject to confidentiality under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-808(2)(b)(ii): shall authorize the Department of Workforce Services to disclose to the office the employment data that the life science establishment submits to the Department of Workforce Services;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-808(2)(b)(iii): shall require the life science establishment to provide the office with the life science establishment's current capitalization tables; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-808(2)(b)(iv): may require the life science establishment to provide the office with other data that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-808(2)(b)(iv)(A): ensure compliance with the requirements of this chapter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-2-808(2)(b)(iv)(B): demonstrate the economic impact of the tax credit applicant's investment in the life science establishment.
