Utah Code Annotated - Title 63N - Chapter 3 - Economic Development Programs
***************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-101 Title -- Purpose.
-------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-101(1): This chapter is known as "Economic Development Programs."
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-101(2): This part is known as the "Industrial Assistance Account."
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-101(3): The Legislature finds and declares that the fostering and development of industry in Utah is a state public purpose necessary to assure the welfare of its citizens, the growth of its economy, and adequate employment for its citizens.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-102 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-102(1): "Administrator" means the executive director or the executive director's designee.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-102(2): "Applicant" means an individual, for profit business entity, nonprofit, corporation, partnership, unincorporated association, government entity, executive branch department or division of a department, a political subdivision, a state institution of higher education, or any other administrative unit of the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-102(3): "Economic opportunities" means business situations or community circumstances which lend themselves to the furtherance of the economic interests of the state by providing a catalyst or stimulus to the growth or retention, or both, of commerce and industry in the state, including retention of companies whose relocation outside the state would have a significant detrimental economic impact on the state as a whole, regions of the state, or specific components of the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-102(4): 63N-3-103 "Restricted Account" means the restricted account known as the Industrial Assistance Account created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-102(5): 63N-3-112 "Talent development grant" means a grant awarded under Section


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-103 Industrial Assistance Account created -- Uses -- Administrator duties -- Costs.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-103(1): There is created a restricted account within the General Fund known as the "Industrial Assistance Account".
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-103(2): The administrator shall administer the restricted account.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-103(3): The administrator may hire appropriate support staff to perform the duties required under this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-103(4): The cost of administering the restricted account shall be paid from money in the restricted account.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-103(5): Interest accrued from investment of money in the restricted account shall remain in the restricted account.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-103(6): 63N-1a-306 The office shall review the activities and progress of grant recipients under this chapter on a regular basis and, as part of the office's annual written report described in Section


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-105 Qualification for assistance -- Application requirements.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-105(1): Subject to the requirements of this part, the administrator may provide loans, grants, or other financial assistance from the restricted account to an entity offering an economic opportunity if that entity:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-105(1)(a): applies to the administrator in a form approved by the administrator; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-105(1)(b): meets the qualifications of Subsection (2).
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-105(2): As part of an application for receiving financial assistance under this part, an applicant shall demonstrate the following to the satisfaction of the administrator:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-105(2)(a): the nature of the economic opportunity and the related benefit to the economic well-being of the state by providing evidence documenting the expenditure of money necessitated by the economic opportunity;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-105(2)(b): how the economic opportunity will act in concert with other state, federal, or local agencies to achieve the economic benefit;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-105(2)(c): that the applicant will expend funds in the state with employees, vendors, subcontractors, or other businesses in an amount proportional with money provided from the restricted account at a minimum ratio of one to one per year or other more stringent requirements as established on a per project basis by the administrator;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-105(2)(d): for an application for a loan, the applicant's ability to sustain economic activity in the state sufficient to repay, by means of cash or appropriate credits, the loan provided by the restricted account; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-105(2)(e): any other criteria the administrator considers appropriate.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-105(3): 63N-3-106
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-105(3)(a): The administrator may exempt an applicant from any of the requirements of Subsection (2) if:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-105(3)(a)(i): the applicant is part of a targeted industry; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-105(3)(a)(ii): the applicant is a quasi-public corporation organized under Title 16, Chapter 6a, Utah Revised Nonprofit Corporation Act, or Title 63E, Chapter 2, Independent Corporations Act, and the applicant's operations, as demonstrated to the satisfaction of the administrator, will provide significant economic stimulus to the growth of commerce and industry in the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-105(3)(b): 63N-3-106 The administrator may not exempt the applicant from the requirement under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-105(4): 63N-3-107 Before awarding any money under this part, the administrator shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-105(4)(a): make findings as to whether an applicant has satisfied the requirements of Subsection (2);
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-105(4)(b): establish benchmarks and timeframes in which progress toward the completion of the agreed upon activity is to occur;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-105(4)(c): 63N-3-107 monitor compliance by an applicant with any contract or agreement entered into by the applicant and the state as provided by Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-105(4)(d): make funding decisions based upon appropriate findings and compliance.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-106 Structure of loans, grants, and assistance -- Repayment -- Earned credits.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-106(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-106(1)(a): Subject to Subsection (1)(b), the administrator has authority to determine the structure, amount, and nature of any loan, grant, or other financial assistance from the restricted account.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-106(1)(b): Loans made under this part shall be structured so the intended repayment or return to the state, including cash or credit, equals at least the amount of the assistance together with an annual interest charge as negotiated by the administrator.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-106(1)(c): Payments resulting from grants awarded from the restricted account shall be made only after the administrator has determined that the company has satisfied the conditions upon which the payment or earned credit was based.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-106(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-106(2)(a): The administrator may provide for a system of earned credits that may be used to support grant payments or in lieu of cash repayment of a restricted account loan obligation.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-106(2)(b): The value of the credits described in Subsection (2)(a) shall be based on factors determined by the administrator, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-106(2)(b)(i): the number of Utah jobs created;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-106(2)(b)(ii): the increased economic activity in Utah; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-106(2)(b)(iii): other events and activities that occur as a result of the restricted account assistance.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-106(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-106(3)(a): A cash loan repayment or other cash recovery from a company receiving assistance under this section, including interest, shall be deposited into the restricted account.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-106(3)(b): The administrator and the Division of Finance shall determine the manner of recognizing and accounting for the earned credits used in lieu of loan repayments or to support grant payments as provided in Subsection (2).
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-106(4): 63J-1-312; 63J-1-315; 63J-1-312; 63J-1-314
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-106(4)(a): 63J-1-312

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-106(4)(b): 63J-1-315; 63J-1-312; 63J-1-314 The Division of Finance shall make the transfer required by Subsection (4)(a) after the Division of Finance transfers the General Fund revenue surplusto:

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-111 Annual policy considerations.
-------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-111(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-111(1)(a): The office shall make recommendations to state and federal agencies, local governments, the governor, and the Legislature regarding policies and initiatives that promote the economic development of targeted industries.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-111(1)(b): The office may create one or more voluntary advisory committees that may include public and private stakeholders to solicit input on policy guidance and best practices in encouraging the economic development of targeted industries.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-111(2): 63N-3-105 The administrator may establish:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-111(2)(a): minimum interest rates to be applied to loans granted that reflect a fair social rate of return to the state comparable to prevailing market-based rates such as the prime rate, U.S. Government T-bill rate, or bond coupon rate as paid by the state, adjusted by social indicators such as the rate of unemployment; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-111(2)(b): 63N-3-105 minimum applicant expense ratios, as long as they are at least equal to those required under Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-112 Talent development grants.
----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-112(1): A for-profit business that is creating new incremental high paying jobs in the state, may apply to receive a talent development grant from the restricted account.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-112(2): In accordance with the provisions of this section and in consultation with the GOEO board, the administrator may award up to $10,000 per new job created.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-112(3): The administrator shall designate an application process for a business to apply for the grant.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-112(4): A business may apply to receive a grant only after each employee has been employed at qualifying wage levels for at least 12 consecutive months.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-112(5): The office shall deduct money granted for a talent development grant under this section from any other money or incentive awarded by the office to the business.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-112(6): Grants awarded under this section are only to reimburse a business for the costs incurred to recruit, hire, train, and otherwise employ an employee in a newly created job.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-112(7): As part of the application process, a business shall submit a hiring and training plan detailing how the grant money will be used.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-112(8): The administrator may grant an award only up to an amount that is no more than 25% of the estimated costs to be incurred by the business for the costs in the hiring and training plan.

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-113(2)(a): describe the activities the entity will undertake to provide technical assistance to a municipality in connection with planning for housing, transportation, and growth; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-113(2)(b): satisfy other criteria the administrator considers appropriate.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-113(3): (2); 63N-3-107 Before awarding any money under this section, the administrator shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-113(3)(a): (2) make findings as to whether an applicant has satisfied the requirements of Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-601 Title.
--------------------------------------
This part is known as the "Housing and Transit Reinvestment Zone Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-602 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-602(1): "Affordable housing" means housing occupied or reserved for occupancy by households with a gross household income:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-602(1)(a): equal to or less than 80% of the median gross income of the applicable municipal or county statistical area for households of the same size, in certain circumstances as provided in this part; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-602(1)(b): equal to or less than 60% of the median gross income of the applicable municipal or county statistical area for households of the same size, in certain circumstances as provided in this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-602(2): 17C-1-102 "Agency" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-602(3): "Base taxable value" means a property's taxable value as shown upon the assessment roll last equalized during the base year.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-602(4): "Base year" means, for each tax increment collection period triggered within a proposed housing and transit reinvestment zone area, the calendar year prior to the calendar year the tax increment begins to be collected for those parcels triggered for that collection period.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-602(5): "Bus rapid transit" means a high-quality bus-based transit system that delivers fast and efficient service that may include dedicated lanes, busways, traffic signal priority, off-board fare collection, elevated platforms, and enhanced stations.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-602(6): "Bus rapid transit station" means an existing station, stop, or terminal, or a proposed station, stop, or terminal that is specifically identified as needed in phase one of a metropolitan planning organization's adopted long-range transportation plan and in phase one of the relevant public transit district's adopted long-range transit plan:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-602(6)(a): along an existing bus rapid transit line; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-602(6)(b): along an extension to an existing bus rapid transit line or new bus rapid transit line.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-602(7): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-602(7)(a): "Commuter rail" means a heavy-rail passenger rail transit facility operated by a large public transit district.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-602(7)(b): "Commuter rail" does not include a light-rail passenger rail facility of a large public transit district.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-602(8): "Commuter rail station" means an existing station, stop, or terminal, or a proposed station, stop, or terminal, which has been specifically identified as needed in phase one of a metropolitan planning organization's adopted long-range transportation plan and in phase one of the relevant public transit district's adopted long-range transit plan:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-602(8)(a): along an existing commuter rail line;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-602(8)(b): along an extension to an existing commuter rail line or new commuter rail line; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-602(8)(c): along a fixed guideway extension from an existing commuter rail line.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-602(9): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-602(9)(a): "Developable area" means the portion of land within a housing and transit reinvestment zone available for development and construction of business and residential uses.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-602(9)(b): "Developable area" does not include portions of land within a housing and transit reinvestment zone that are allocated to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-602(9)(b)(i): parks;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-602(9)(b)(ii): recreation facilities;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-602(9)(b)(iii): open space;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-602(9)(b)(iv): trails;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-602(9)(b)(v): publicly-owned roadway facilities; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-602(9)(b)(vi): other public facilities.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-602(10): "Dwelling unit" means one or more rooms arranged for the use of one or more individuals living together, as a single housekeeping unit normally having cooking, living, sanitary, and sleeping facilities.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-602(11): "Enhanced development" means the construction of mixed uses including housing, commercial uses, and related facilities.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-602(12): "Enhanced development costs" means extra costs associated with structured parking costs, vertical construction costs, horizontal construction costs, life safety costs, structural costs, conveyor or elevator costs, and other costs incurred due to the increased height of buildings or enhanced development.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-602(13): 63N-3-1601 "First home investment zone" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-602(14): 59-12-102 "Fixed guideway" means the same as that term is defined in Section

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603 Applicability, requirements, and limitations on a housing and transit reinvestment zone.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(1): 10-9a-403 A housing and transit reinvestment zone proposal created under this part shall promote the following objectives:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(1)(a): higher utilization of public transit;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(1)(b): increasing availability of housing, including affordable housing, and fulfillment of moderate income housing plans;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(1)(c): promoting and encouraging development of owner-occupied housing;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(1)(d): improving efficiencies in parking and transportation, including walkability of communities near public transit facilities;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(1)(e): overcoming development impediments and market conditions that render a development cost prohibitive absent the proposal and incentives;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(1)(f): conserving water resources through efficient land use;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(1)(g): improving air quality by reducing fuel consumption and motor vehicle trips;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(1)(h): encouraging transformative mixed-use development and investment in transportation and public transit infrastructure in strategic areas;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(1)(i): 10-9a-403 strategic land use and municipal planning in major transit investment corridors as described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(1)(j): increasing access to employment and educational opportunities; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(1)(k): increasing access to child care.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(2)(a): In order to accomplish the objectives described in Subsection (1), a municipality or public transit county that initiates the process to create a housing and transit reinvestment zone as described in this part shall ensure that the proposal for a housing and transit reinvestment zone includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(2)(a)(i): except as provided in Subsection (3), at least 12% of the proposed dwelling units within the housing and transit reinvestment zone are affordable housing units, with:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(2)(a)(i)(A): up to 9% of the proposed dwelling units occupied or reserved for occupancy by households with a gross household income equal to or less than 80% of the median gross income of the applicable municipal or county statistical area for households of the same size; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(2)(a)(i)(B): at least 3% of the proposed dwelling units occupied or reserved for occupancy by households with a gross household income equal to or less than 60% of the median gross income of the applicable municipal or county statistical area for households of the same size;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(2)(a)(ii): except as provided in Subsection (2)(c), a housing and transit reinvestment zone shall include:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(2)(a)(ii)(A): at least 51% of the developable area within a housing and transit reinvestment zone as residential uses; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(2)(a)(ii)(B): an average of at least 50 dwelling units per acre within the acreage of the housing and transit reinvestment zone dedicated to residential uses;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(2)(a)(iii): mixed-use development; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(2)(a)(iv): a mix of dwelling units to ensure that a reasonable percentage of the dwelling units has more than one bedroom.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(2)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(2)(b)(i): If a housing and transit reinvestment zone is phased, a municipality or public transit county shall ensure that a housing and transit reinvestment zone is phased and developed to provide the required 12% of affordable housing units in each phase of development.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(2)(b)(ii): A municipality or public transit county may allow a housing and transit reinvestment zone to be phased and developed in a manner to provide more of the required affordable housing units in early phases of development.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(2)(b)(iii): A municipality or public transit county shall include in a housing and transit reinvestment zone proposal an affordable housing plan, which may include deed restrictions, to ensure the affordable housing required in the proposal will continue to meet the definition of affordable housing at least throughout the entire term of the housing and transit reinvestment zone.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(2)(c): For a housing and transit reinvestment zone proposed by a public transit county at a public transit hub, or for a housing and transit reinvestment zone proposed by a municipality at a bus rapid transit station, the housing and transit reinvestment zone shall include:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(2)(c)(i): at least 51% of the developable area within a housing and transit reinvestment zone as residential uses; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(2)(c)(ii): an average of at least 39 dwelling units per acre within the acreage of the housing and transit reinvestment zone dedicated to residential uses.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(3): A municipality or public transit county that, at the time the housing and transit reinvestment zone proposal is approved by the housing and transit reinvestment zone committee, meets the affordable housing guidelines of the United States Department of Housing and Urban Development at 60% area median income is exempt from the requirement described in Subsection (2)(a).
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(4): 63N-3-607; 63N-3-607; 17C-1-102; 17C-1-102
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(4)(a): 63N-3-607 A municipality may only propose a housing and transit reinvestment zone at a commuter rail station, and a public transit county may only propose a housing and transit reinvestment zone at a public transit hub, that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(4)(a)(i): subject to Subsection (5)(a):
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(4)(a)(i)(A): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(4)(a)(i)(A)(I): except as provided in Subsection (4)(a)(i)(A)(II), for a municipality, does not exceed a 1/3 mile radius of a commuter rail station;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(4)(a)(i)(A)(II): for a municipality that is a city of the first class with a population greater than 150,000 that is within a county of the first class, with an opportunity zone created pursuant to Section 1400Z-1, Internal Revenue Code, does not exceed a 1/2 mile radius of a commuter rail station located within the opportunity zone; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(4)(a)(i)(A)(III): for a public transit county, does not exceed a 1/3 mile radius of a public transit hub; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(4)(a)(i)(B): has a total area of no more than 125 noncontiguous acres;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(4)(a)(ii): 63N-3-607 subject to Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(4)(a)(iii): the commencement of collection of tax increment, for all or a portion of the housing and transit reinvestment zone, will be triggered by providing notice as described in Subsection (6), but a housing and transit reinvestment zone proposal may not propose or include triggering more than three tax increment collection periods during the applicable 45-year period.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(4)(b): 63N-3-607 A municipality or public transit county may only propose a housing and transit reinvestment zone at a light rail station or bus rapid transit station that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(4)(b)(i): subject to Subsection (5):
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(4)(b)(i)(A): does not exceed:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(4)(b)(i)(A)(I): except as provided in Subsection (4)(b)(i)(A)(II), (III), or (4)(e), a 1/4 mile radius of a bus rapid transit station or light rail station;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(4)(b)(i)(A)(II): for a municipality that is a city of the first class with a population greater than 150,000 that is within a county of the first class, a 1/2 mile radius of a light rail station located in an opportunity zone created pursuant to Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(4)(b)(i)(A)(III): a 1/2 mile radius of a light rail station located within a master-planned development of 500 acres or more; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(4)(b)(i)(B): has a total area of no more than 100 noncontiguous acres;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(4)(b)(ii): 63N-3-607 subject to Subsection (4)(c) and Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(4)(b)(iii): the commencement of collection of tax increment, for all or a portion of the housing and transit reinvestment zone, will be triggered by providing notice as described in Subsection (6), but a housing and transit reinvestment zone proposal may not propose or include triggering more than three tax increment collection periods during the applicable 30-year period.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(4)(c): For a housing and transit reinvestment zone proposed by a public transit county at a public transit hub, or for a housing and transit reinvestment zone proposed by a municipality at a bus rapid transit station, if the proposed housing density within the housing and transit reinvestment zone is between 39 and 49 dwelling units per acre, the maximum capture of each taxing entity's tax increment above the base year is 60%.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(4)(d): A municipality that is a city of the first class with a population greater than 150,000 in a county of the first class as described in Subsections (4)(a)(i)(A)(II) and (4)(b)(i)(A)(II) may only propose one housing and transit reinvestment zone within an opportunity zone.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(4)(e): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(4)(e)(i): Subject to Subsection (4)(e)(ii), the radius restrictions described in Subsection (4)(b)(i) do not apply, and a housing and transit reinvestment zone may extend to an area between two light rail stations located within a city of the third class if the two light rail stations are within a .95 mile distance on the same light rail line.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(4)(e)(ii): If a housing and transit reinvestment zone is extended to accommodate two light rail stations as described in Subsection (4)(e)(i):
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(4)(e)(ii)(A): the housing and transit reinvestment zone is limited to a total area not to exceed 100 noncontiguous acres; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(4)(e)(ii)(B): the housing and transit reinvestment zone may not exceed a 1/4 mile radius from the light rail stations or any point on the light rail line between the two stations.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(4)(f): 17C-1-102; 17C-1-102 If a parcel within the housing and transit reinvestment zone is included as an area that is part of a project area, as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(5)(a): For a housing and transit reinvestment zone for a commuter rail station, if a parcel is bisected by the relevant radius limitation, the full parcel may be included as part of the housing and transit reinvestment zone area and will not count against the limitations described in Subsection (4)(a)(i).
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(5)(b): For a housing and transit reinvestment zone for a light rail or bus rapid transit station, if a parcel is bisected by the relevant radius limitation, the full parcel may be included as part of the housing and transit reinvestment zone area and will not count against the limitations described in Subsection (4)(b)(i).
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(5)(c): A housing and transit reinvestment zone may not be smaller than 10 acres.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(6): The notice of commencement of collection of tax increment required in Subsection (4)(a)(iii) or (4)(b)(iii) shall be sent by mail or electronically to the following entities no later than January 1 of the year for which the tax increment collection is proposed to commence:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(6)(a): the tax commission;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(6)(b): the State Board of Education;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(6)(c): the state auditor;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(6)(d): the auditor of the county in which the housing and transit reinvestment zone is located;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(6)(e): each taxing entity affected by the collection of tax increment from the housing and transit reinvestment zone; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(6)(f): the Governor's Office of Economic Opportunity.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(7): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(7)(a): The maximum number of housing and transit reinvestment zones at light rail stations is eight in any given county.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(7)(b): Within a county of the first class, the maximum number of housing and transit reinvestment zones at bus rapid transit stations is three.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(7)(c): Within a county of the first class, the maximum total combined number of housing and transit reinvestment zones described in Subsections (7)(a) and (b) and first home investment zones created under Part 16, First Home Investment Zone Act, is 11.

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(8)(c): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(8)(c)(i): A county described in Subsection (8)(a) may not propose a housing and transit reinvestment zone if more than 15% of the acreage within the housing and transit reinvestment zone boundary is owned by the county.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(8)(c)(ii): For purposes of determining the percentage of acreage owned by the county as described in Subsection (8)(c)(i), a county may exclude any acreage owned that is used for highways, bus rapid transit, light rail, or commuter rail within the boundary of the housing and transit reinvestment zone.

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-603(8)(d)(iii): any other infrastructure element necessary or reasonable to support the mixed-use development, including parking infrastructure, streets, sidewalks, parks, and trails.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-604 Process for a proposal of a housing and transit reinvestment zone -- Analysis.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-604(1): 63N-3-605; 63N-3-603; 63N-3-603; 63N-3-610; 63N-3-603; 63N-3-610; 63N-3-603 Subject to approval of the housing and transit reinvestment zone committee as described in Section

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-604(1)(a)(i): 63N-3-603 demonstrates that the proposed housing and transit reinvestment zone will meet the objectives described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-604(1)(a)(ii): 63N-3-603 explains how the municipality or public transit county will achieve the requirements of Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-604(1)(a)(iii): defines the specific transportation infrastructure needs, if any, and proposed improvements;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-604(1)(a)(iv): 63N-3-610 defines the boundaries of:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-604(1)(a)(iv)(A): the housing and transit reinvestment zone; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-604(1)(a)(iv)(B): 63N-3-610 the sales and use tax boundary corresponding to the housing and transit reinvestment zone boundary, as described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-604(1)(a)(v): includes maps of the proposed housing and transit reinvestment zone to illustrate:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-604(1)(a)(v)(A): the proposed boundary and radius from a public transit hub;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-604(1)(a)(v)(B): proposed housing density within the housing and transit reinvestment zone; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-604(1)(a)(v)(C): existing zoning and proposed zoning changes related to the housing and transit reinvestment zone;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-604(1)(a)(vi): identifies any development impediments that prevent the development from being a market-rate investment and proposed strategies for addressing each one;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-604(1)(a)(vii): 63N-3-603 describes the proposed development plan, including the requirements described in Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-604(1)(a)(viii): establishes a base year and collection period to calculate the tax increment within the housing and transit reinvestment zone;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-604(1)(a)(ix): 63N-3-610 establishes a sales and use tax base year to calculate the sales and use tax increment within the housing and transit reinvestment zone in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-604(1)(a)(x): describes projected maximum revenues generated and the amount of tax increment capture from each taxing entity and proposed expenditures of revenue derived from the housing and transit reinvestment zone;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-604(1)(a)(xi): includes an analysis of other applicable or eligible incentives, grants, or sources of revenue that can be used to reduce the finance gap;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-604(1)(a)(xii): evaluates possible benefits to active and public transportation availability and impacts on air quality;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-604(1)(a)(xiii): proposes a finance schedule to align expected revenue with required financing costs and payments;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-604(1)(a)(xiv): 63N-3-603 provides a pro-forma for the planned development that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-604(1)(a)(xiv)(A): 63N-3-603 satisfies the requirements described in Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-604(1)(a)(xiv)(B): includes data showing the cost difference between what type of development could feasibly be developed absent the housing and transit reinvestment zone tax increment and the type of development that is proposed to be developed with the housing and transit reinvestment zone tax increment; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-604(1)(a)(xv): for a housing and transit reinvestment zone at a commuter rail station, light rail station, or bus rapid transit station that is proposed and not in public transit service operation as of the date of submission of the proposal, demonstrates that the proposed station is:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-604(1)(a)(xv)(A): included as needed in phase one of a metropolitan planning organization's adopted long-range transportation plan and in phase one of the relevant public transit district's adopted long-range plan; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-604(1)(a)(xv)(B): reasonably anticipated to be constructed in the near future; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-604(1)(b): submit the housing and transit reinvestment zone proposal to the Governor's Office of Economic Opportunity.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-604(2): As part of the proposal described in Subsection (1), a municipality or public transit county shall study and evaluate possible impacts of a proposed housing and transit reinvestment zone on parking within the city and housing and transit reinvestment zone.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-604(3): 63N-3-603
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-604(3)(a): After receiving the proposal as described in Subsection (1)(b), the Governor's Office of Economic Opportunity shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-604(3)(a)(i): within 14 days after the date on which the Governor's Office of Economic Opportunity receives the proposal described in Subsection (1)(b), provide notice of the proposal to all affected taxing entities, including the Tax Commission, cities, counties, school districts, metropolitan planning organizations, and the county assessor and county auditor of the county in which the housing and transit reinvestment zone is located; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-604(3)(a)(ii): at the expense of the proposing municipality or public transit county as described in Subsection (5), contract with an independent entity to perform the gap analysis described in Subsection (3)(b).
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-604(3)(b): 63N-3-603 The gap analysis required in Subsection (3)(a)(ii) shall include:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-604(3)(b)(i): a description of the planned development;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-604(3)(b)(ii): a market analysis relative to other comparable project developments included in or adjacent to the municipality or public transit county absent the proposed housing and transit reinvestment zone;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-604(3)(b)(iii): an evaluation of the proposal to and a determination of the adequacy and efficiency of the proposal;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-604(3)(b)(iv): an evaluation of the proposed increment capture needed to cover the enhanced development costs associated with the housing and transit reinvestment zone proposal and enable the proposed development to occur; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-604(3)(b)(v): 63N-3-603 based on the market analysis and other findings, an opinion relative to the appropriate amount of potential public financing reasonably determined to be necessary to achieve the objectives described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-604(3)(c): After receiving notice from the Governor's Office of Economic Opportunity of a proposed housing and transit reinvestment zone as described in Subsection (3)(a)(i), the Tax Commission shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-604(3)(c)(i): evaluate the feasibility of administering the tax implications of the proposal; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-604(3)(c)(ii): provide a letter to the Governor's Office of Economic Opportunity describing any challenges in the administration of the proposal, or indicating that the Tax Commission can feasibly administer the proposal.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-604(4): After receiving the results from the analysis described in Subsection (3)(b), the municipality or public transit county proposing the housing and transit reinvestment zone may:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-604(4)(a): amend the housing and transit reinvestment zone proposal based on the findings of the analysis described in Subsection (3)(b) and request that the Governor's Office of Economic Opportunity submit the amended housing and transit reinvestment zone proposal to the housing and transit reinvestment zone committee; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-604(4)(b): request that the Governor's Office of Economic Opportunity submit the original housing and transit reinvestment zone proposal to the housing and transit reinvestment zone committee.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-604(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-604(5)(a): The Governor's Office of Economic Opportunity may accept, as a dedicated credit, up to $20,000 from a municipality or public transit county for the costs of the gap analysis described in Subsection (3)(b).
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-604(5)(b): The Governor's Office of Economic Opportunity may expend funds received from a municipality or public transit county as dedicated credits to pay for the costs associated with the gap analysis described in Subsection (3)(b).


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-605 Housing and Transit Reinvestment Zone Committee -- Creation.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-605(1): For any housing and transit reinvestment zone proposed under this part, or for a first home investment zone proposed in accordance with Part 16, First Home Investment Zone Act, there is created a housing and transit reinvestment zone committee with membership described in Subsection (2).
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-605(2): 72-1-301 Each housing and transit reinvestment zone committee shall consist of the following members:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-605(2)(a): one representative from the Governor's Office of Economic Opportunity, designated by the executive director of the Governor's Office of Economic Opportunity;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-605(2)(b): one representative from each municipality that is a party to the proposed housing and transit reinvestment zone or first home investment zone, designated by the chief executive officer of each respective municipality;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-605(2)(c): 72-1-301 a member of the Transportation Commission created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-605(2)(d): a member of the board of trustees of a large public transit district;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-605(2)(e): one individual from the Office of the State Treasurer, designated by the state treasurer;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-605(2)(f): two members designated by the president of the Senate;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-605(2)(g): two members designated by the speaker of the House of Representatives;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-605(2)(h): one member designated by the chief executive officer of each county affected by the housing and transit reinvestment zone or first home investment zone;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-605(2)(i): two representatives designated by the school superintendent from the school district affected by the housing and transit reinvestment zone or first home investment zone; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-605(2)(j): one representative, representing the largest participating local taxing entity, after the municipality, county, and school district.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-605(3): The individual designated by the Governor's Office of Economic Opportunity as described in Subsection (2)(a) shall serve as chair of the housing and transit reinvestment zone committee.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-605(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-605(4)(a): A majority of the members of the housing and transit reinvestment zone committee constitutes a quorum of the housing and transit reinvestment zone committee.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-605(4)(b): An action by a majority of a quorum of the housing and transit reinvestment zone committee is an action of the housing and transit reinvestment zone committee.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-605(5): 63N-3-604; 63N-3-1604
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-605(5)(a): 63N-3-604 After the Governor's Office of Economic Opportunity receives the results of the analysis described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-605(5)(b): 63N-3-1604 For a first home investment zone, the housing and transit reinvestment zone committee shall follow the procedures described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-605(6): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-605(6)(a): The chair of the housing and transit reinvestment zone committee shall convene a public meeting to consider the proposed housing and transit reinvestment zone.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-605(6)(b): A meeting of the housing and transit reinvestment zone committee is subject to Title 52, Chapter 4, Open and Public Meetings Act.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-605(7): 63N-3-603; 63N-3-604

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-605(9): If a housing and transit reinvestment zone is approved by the committee:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-605(9)(a): the proposed housing and transit reinvestment zone is established according to the terms of the housing and transit reinvestment zone proposal;

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-605(9)(c): each affected taxing entity is required to participate at the same rate .
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-605(10): A housing and transit reinvestment zone proposal may be amended by following the same procedure as approving a housing and transit reinvestment zone proposal.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-606 Notice requirements.
----------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-606(1): In approving a housing and transit reinvestment zone proposal the housing and transit reinvestment zone committee shall follow the hearing and notice requirements for creating a housing and transit reinvestment zone area proposal.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-606(2): 63A-16-505 Within 30 days after the housing and transit reinvestment zone committee approves a proposed housing and transit reinvestment zone, the municipality or public transit county shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-606(2)(a): record with the recorder of the county in which the housing and transit reinvestment zone is located a document containing:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-606(2)(a)(i): a description of the land within the housing and transit reinvestment zone;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-606(2)(a)(ii): a statement that the proposed housing and transit reinvestment zone has been approved; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-606(2)(a)(iii): the date of adoption;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-606(2)(b): 63A-16-505 transmit a copy of the description of the land within the housing and transit reinvestment zone and an accurate map or plat indicating the boundaries of the housing and transit reinvestment zone to the Utah Geospatial Resource Center created under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-606(2)(c): transmit a copy of the approved housing and transit reinvestment zone proposal, map, and description of the land within the housing and transit reinvestment zone, to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-606(2)(c)(i): the auditor, recorder, attorney, surveyor, and assessor of the county in which any part of the housing and transit reinvestment zone is located;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-606(2)(c)(ii): the officer or officers performing the function of auditor or assessor for each taxing entity that does not use the county assessment roll or collect the taxing entity's taxes through the county;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-606(2)(c)(iii): the legislative body or governing board of each taxing entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-606(2)(c)(iv): the tax commission; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-606(2)(c)(v): the State Board of Education.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-607 Payment, use, and administration of revenue from a housing and transit reinvestment zone.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-607(1): A municipality or public transit county may receive and use tax increment and housing and transit reinvestment zone funds in accordance with this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-607(2): 59-2-1365; 63N-3-603
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-607(2)(a): 59-2-1365 A county that collects property tax on property located within a housing and transit reinvestment zone shall, in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-607(2)(b): Tax increment distributed to a municipality or public transit county in accordance with Subsection (2)(a) is not revenue of the taxing entity or municipality or public transit county.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-607(2)(c): 63N-3-603
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-607(2)(c)(i): Tax increment paid to the municipality or public transit county are housing and transit reinvestment zone funds and shall be administered by an agency created by the municipality or public transit county within which the housing and transit reinvestment zone is located.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-607(2)(c)(ii): 63N-3-603 Before an agency may receive housing and transit reinvestment zone funds from the municipality or public transit county, the municipality or public transit county and the agency shall enter into an interlocal agreement with terms that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-607(2)(c)(ii)(A): are consistent with the approval of the housing and transit reinvestment zone committee; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-607(2)(c)(ii)(B): 63N-3-603 meet the requirements of Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-607(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-607(3)(a): A municipality or public transit county and agency shall use housing and transit reinvestment zone funds within, or for the direct benefit of, the housing and transit reinvestment zone.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-607(3)(b): If any housing and transit reinvestment zone funds will be used outside of the housing and transit reinvestment zone there must be a finding in the approved proposal for a housing and transit reinvestment zone that the use of the housing and transit reinvestment zone funds outside of the housing and transit reinvestment zone will directly benefit the housing and transit reinvestment zone.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-607(4): 63N-3-603; 63N-3-604 A municipality or public transit county shall use housing and transit reinvestment zone funds to achieve the purposes described in Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-607(4)(a): income targeted housing costs;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-607(4)(b): structured parking within the housing and transit reinvestment zone;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-607(4)(c): enhanced development costs;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-607(4)(d): horizontal construction costs;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-607(4)(e): vertical construction costs;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-607(4)(f): property acquisition costs within the housing and transit reinvestment zone; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-607(4)(g): 63N-3-604 the costs of the municipality or public transit county to create and administer the housing and transit reinvestment zone, which may not exceed 2% of the total housing and transit reinvestment zone funds, plus the costs to complete the gap analysis described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-607(5): Housing and transit reinvestment zone funds may be paid to a participant, if the agency and participant enter into a participation agreement which requires the participant to utilize the housing and transit reinvestment zone funds as allowed in this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-607(6): Housing and transit reinvestment zone funds may be used to pay all of the costs of bonds issued by the municipality or public transit county in accordance with Title 17C, Chapter 1, Part 5, Agency Bonds, including the cost to issue and repay the bonds including interest.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-607(7): A municipality or public transit county may create one or more public infrastructure districts within the housing and transit reinvestment zone under Title 17D, Chapter 4, Public Infrastructure District Act, and pledge and utilize the housing and transit reinvestment zone funds to guarantee the payment of public infrastructure bonds issued by a public infrastructure district.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-608 Applicability to an existing community reinvestment project.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
For a housing and transit reinvestment zone created under this part that overlaps any portion of an existing inactive industrial site community reinvestment project area plan created pursuant toUtah Code Annotated § 63N-3-608(1): if the community reinvestment project area plan captures less than 80% of the tax increment from a taxing entity, or if a taxing entity is not participating in the community reinvestment project area plan, the housing and transit reinvestment zone may capture the difference between:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-608(1)(a): 80%; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-608(1)(b): the percentage of tax increment captured pursuant to the community reinvestment project area plan; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-608(2): if a community reinvestment project area plan expires before the housing and transit reinvestment zone, the housing and transit reinvestment zone may capture the tax increment allocated to the community reinvestment project area plan for any remaining portion of the term of the housing and transit reinvestment zone.

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-609(1)(b)(ii): the housing and transit reinvestment zone has no binding financial obligations.

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-610 Sales and use tax increment in a housing and transit reinvestment zone.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-610(1): A housing and transit reinvestment proposal shall, in consultation with the tax commission:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-610(1)(a): create a sales and use tax boundary as described in Subsection (2); and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-610(1)(b): establish a sales and use tax base year and collection period to calculate and transfer the state sales and use tax increment within the housing and transit reinvestment zone, which sales and use tax base year is established prospectively, 90 days after the date of the notice described in Subsection (4).
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-610(2): 59-12-102; 63N-3-604
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-610(2)(a): 59-12-102 The municipality or public transit county, in consultation with the tax commission, shall establish a sales and use tax boundary that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-610(2)(a)(i): 59-12-102 is based on state sales and use tax collection boundaries, which are determined using the ZIP Code as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-610(2)(a)(ii): follows as closely as reasonably practicable the boundary of the housing and transit reinvestment zone; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-610(2)(a)(iii): is one contiguous area that includes at least the entire boundary of the housing and transit reinvestment zone.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-610(2)(b): If a state sales and use tax boundary is bisected by the boundary of the housing and transit reinvestment zone, the housing and transit reinvestment zone may include the entire state sales and use tax boundary.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-610(2)(c): 63N-3-604 The municipality or public transit county shall include the sales and use tax boundary in the housing and transit reinvestment zone proposal as described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-610(3): 72-2-124
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-610(3)(a): 72-2-124 Beginning the first day of the calendar quarter one year after the sales and use tax boundary for a housing and transit reinvestment zone is established, the tax commission shall, at least annually, transfer an amount equal to 15% of the sales and use tax increment within an established sales and use tax boundary into the Transit Transportation Investment Fund created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-610(3)(b): A municipality or public transit county may only propose one sales and use tax increment period for a housing and transit reinvestment zone established under this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-610(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-610(4)(a): The establishment of a sales and use tax base year and the requirement described in Subsection (3) to transfer incremental sales tax revenue shall take effect:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-610(4)(a)(i): on the first day of a calendar quarter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-610(4)(a)(ii): after a 90-day waiting period, beginning on the date the commission receives notice from the municipality or public transit county meeting the requirements of Subsection (4)(b).

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-611 Boundary adjustments.
-----------------------------------------------------
If the relevant county assessor or county auditor adjusts parcel boundaries relevant to a housing and transit reinvestment zone, the municipality administering the tax increment collected in the housing and transit reinvestment zone may make corresponding adjustments to the boundary of the housing and transit reinvestment zone.

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-801 Creation and administration.
------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-801(1): There is created an enterprise fund known as the "State Small Business Credit Initiative Program Fund" administered by the office.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-801(2): The executive director or the executive director's designee is the administrator of the fund.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-801(3): Revenues deposited into the fund shall consist of:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-801(3)(a): grants, pay backs, bonuses, entitlements, and other money received from the federal government to implement the State Small Business Credit Initiative; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-801(3)(b): transfers, grants, gifts, bequests, and other money made available from any source to implement this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-801(4): Title 51, Chapter 7, State Money Management Act
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-801(4)(a): Title 51, Chapter 7, State Money Management Act The state treasurer shall invest the money in the fund according to the procedures and requirements of
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-801(4)(b): Interest and other earnings derived from the fund money shall be deposited in the fund.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-801(5): The office may use fund money for administration of the fund.

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-803 Annual accounting.
--------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-803(1): The office shall monitor the activities of recipients of the loans and loan guarantees issued under this part on a yearly basis to ensure compliance with the terms and conditions imposed on the recipient by the office under this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-803(2): An entity receiving a loan or loan guarantee under this part shall provide the office with an annual accounting of how the money it received from the fund was spent.

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-803(3)(b): an evaluation of the effectiveness of the loan and loan guarantee program.

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-902 Strategic Innovation Grant Pilot Program.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-902(1): There is created within the office the Strategic Innovation Grant Pilot Program.

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-902(2)(a): air quality in the state; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-902(2)(b): the conservation or more efficient utilization of water resources in the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-902(3): (2)

Gardner Policy Institute at the University of Utah, the Institute of Land, Water, and Air at Utah State University, or the Bingham Research Center at Utah State University to determine whether the project is meeting:

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1002 Creation of Economic Assistance Grant Program -- Requirements -- Rulemaking -- Annual report.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1002(1): There is created the Economic Assistance Grant Program administered by the office.

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1002(2)(a): promote and support economic opportunities in the state; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1002(2)(b): provide a service in the state related to industry, education, community development, or infrastructure.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1002(3): In awarding grants, the office may prioritize projects:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1002(3)(a): that develop targeted industries in the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1002(3)(b): where an applicant identifies clear metrics to measure the progress, effectiveness, and scope of the project;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1002(3)(c): where an applicant demonstrates comprehensive planning of the project; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1002(3)(d): that require one-time funds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1002(4): Before a business entity may receive a grant, the business entity shall enter into a written agreement with the office that specifies:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1002(4)(a): the amount of the grant;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1002(4)(b): the time period for distributing the grant;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1002(4)(c): the terms and conditions that the business entity shall meet to receive the grant;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1002(4)(d): the structure of the grant; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1002(4)(e): the expenses for which the business entity may expend the grant.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1002(5): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act In accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1002(6): 63N-1a-306 The office shall include in the annual written report described in Section

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1102 Manufacturing Modernization Grant Program -- Creation -- Purpose -- Requirements -- Rulemaking -- Report.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1102(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1102(1)(a): There is created the Manufacturing Modernization Grant Program to be administered by the office.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1102(1)(b): The purpose of the program is to award grants to existing Utah businesses to establish, relocate, retain, or develop manufacturing industry in the state and lessen dependence on manufacturing overseas.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1102(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1102(2)(a): An entity that submits a proposal for a grant to the office shall include details in the proposal regarding:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1102(2)(a)(i): the entity's plan to use the grant to fulfill the purpose described in Subsection (1)(b);
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1102(2)(a)(ii): any plan to use funding sources in addition to a grant for the proposal; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1102(2)(a)(iii): any existing or planned partnerships between the entity and another individual or entity to implement the proposal.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1102(2)(b): In evaluating a proposal for a grant, the office shall consider:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1102(2)(b)(i): the likelihood the proposal will accomplish the purpose described in Subsection (1)(b);
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1102(2)(b)(ii): the extent to which any additional funding sources or existing or planned partnerships will benefit the proposal; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1102(2)(b)(iii): the viability and sustainability of the proposal.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1102(2)(c): In determining a grant award, the office:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1102(2)(c)(i): may consult with the GOEO board; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1102(2)(c)(ii): may prioritize a targeted industry or an entity with fewer than 250 employees.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1102(3): Before receiving the grant, a grant recipient shall enter into a written agreement with the office that specifies:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1102(3)(a): the grant amount;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1102(3)(b): the time period and structure for distribution of the grant, including any terms and conditions the recipient is required to meet to receive a distribution; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1102(3)(c): the expenses for which the recipient may use the grant, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1102(3)(c)(i): acquisition of manufacturing equipment;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1102(3)(c)(ii): production, design, or engineering costs;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1102(3)(c)(iii): specialized employee training;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1102(3)(c)(iv): technology upgrades; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1102(3)(c)(v): provision of a grant to another individual or entity for the expenses described in Subsections (3)(c)(i) through (iv) or to otherwise fulfill the recipient's proposal.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1102(4): Subject to Subsection (2), the office may, in accordance with Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act, make rules to establish:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1102(4)(a): the form and process for submitting a proposal to the office for a grant;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1102(4)(b): the entities that are eligible to apply for a grant;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1102(4)(c): the method and formula for determining a grant amount; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1102(4)(d): the reporting requirements for a grant recipient.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1102(5): On or before October 1 of each year, the office shall provide a written report to the Economic Development and Workforce Services Interim Committee regarding:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1102(5)(a): each grant awarded; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1102(5)(b): the economic impact of each grant.

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1202(1): There is created the Redevelopment Matching Grant Program administered by the office.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1202(2): (3); (4) Subject to appropriations from the Legislature, the office shall award grants to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1202(2)(a): (3) local governments that meet the qualifications described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1202(2)(b): (4) water conservancy districts, special districts, and special service districts that meet the qualifications described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1202(3): To qualify for a grant, a local government shall:

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1202(5): In awarding grants to local governments, the office may award an initial grant to a local government in an amount of up to $2,500,000, and an additional grant of up to $1,500,000, if the project includes a minimum of 1,000 housing units or a minimum of 40 units per acre.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1202(6): The office may not award more than 35% of the total amount of grant funds available for projects to conserve or develop water assets.

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1302(2)(b)(iii): the viability and sustainability of the proposal.

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1302(2)(c)(ii): may prioritize a business that is committed to switching from producing cannabinoid products to industrial hemp products.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1302(3): Before receiving the grant, a grant recipient shall enter into a written agreement with the office that specifies:

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1401(7)(a): provides seating for spectators in a number that is reasonably consistent with the capacity of other stadiums used by other teams in the major professional sports league;

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1402 Project area.
----------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1402(1): 59-12-402.5; 63N-3-1403 A local government may, according to the requirements and procedures of this part, create a project area for the use of revenue authorized under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1402(2): A project area created under this part shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1402(2)(a): be located entirely within the boundaries of the local government;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1402(2)(b): be no greater than 100 acres in area;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1402(2)(c): be roughly centered around, and include the entire property footprint of a currently existing qualified stadium;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1402(2)(d): include the entire property footprint of any qualified stadium that is planned to be built;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1402(2)(e): be contiguous; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1402(2)(f): have boundaries that are reasonably compact in relation to their distance from the currently existing qualified stadium.

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1403(2)(a): costs for, including debt service or the costs of bonds issued by the local government or state:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1403(2)(a)(i): paid to or for the benefit of a project participant for the construction or remodel of a qualified stadium within the project area in accordance with Title 17C, Chapter 1, Part 5, Agency Bonds, including the cost to issue and repay bonds and interest; and

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1404 Application for approval as a project participant in a project area.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
A person that seeks to have a local government create a project area under this part, and to be a project participant within that project area, shall provide a local government with a written application that certifies that the applicant:Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1404(1): is a party to a franchise agreement;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1404(2): is or will be operating the team that is subject to the franchise agreement:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1404(2)(a): in an existing qualified stadium located within the project area to be created; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1404(2)(b): in a new qualified stadium that will be located within the project area;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1404(3): shows the existing and, as applicable, the proposed location and footprint of the qualified stadium;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1404(4): lists any public funds that are currently being received by, or are authorized to be received by:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1404(4)(a): the applicant; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1404(4)(b): any major professional sports league team that is owned or operated by the applicant; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1404(5): any proposals or information related to the application, including specific details about the franchise agreement or plans for a qualified stadium, a proposed boundary for the project area, proposals for land or stadium ownership arrangements or stadium revenue-sharing arrangements, or plans or requests for urban renewal or reconstruction.

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1405(1)(b)(v)(C)(IV): a public safety plan, including plans for mitigating crime and ensuring safety and physical security within the project area;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1405(1)(b)(v)(C)(V): a homelessness mitigation plan, including plans to provide resources for homeless individuals and to mitigate and manage camping and other related social issues within the project area;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1405(1)(b)(v)(C)(VI): a transportation plan, including plans to enable access to and from, and public transportation, vehicle, and pedestrian traffic flow within the project area; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1405(1)(b)(v)(C)(VII): a parking plan, including estimates for parking needs and plans for accommodating those needs within the project area;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1405(1)(b)(vi): a provision that the local government may not provide, and that a project participant may not receive, a direct subsidy;

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1405(1)(b)(viii)(D): designation of a guarantor, security interests, or other measures to ensure repayment of revenue and funds in the event of a breach;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1405(1)(b)(ix): procedures and penalties that apply in the event that the local government or project participant fails to meet requirements, goals, or objectives set under Subsection (1)(b)(v);
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1405(1)(b)(x): an acknowledgment that the parties to the agreement are subject to the requirements of this part;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1405(1)(b)(xi): any additional obligations, terms, or conditions mutually agreed upon by the local government and the project participant; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1405(1)(b)(xii): may contain:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1405(1)(b)(xii)(A): any terms and conditions that affect a project participant's ability to receive or use project area funds;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1405(1)(b)(xii)(B): any terms or agreements regarding the qualified stadium and its associated property, including ownership, management, maintenance, operation, revenue sharing, or other agreements;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1405(1)(b)(xii)(C): terms, procedures, or remedies related to breach of a participation agreement; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1405(1)(b)(xii)(D): any other relevant agreement between the applicant and the local government.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1405(2): Before finalizing a proposed project area under Subsection (3), a local government shall ensure that any zoning modifications or requirements within the project area are complete.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1405(3): If the applicant and the local government develop a proposed project area and a proposed participation agreement as described in Subsection (1), the local government shall, no later than September 1, 2024, provide notice of the proposed agreement and provide a copy of the application, the proposed project area, and the proposed participation agreement to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1405(3)(a): the legislative body of the local government; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1405(3)(b): the Revitalization Zone Committee.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1406 Local government endorsement -- Revitalization Zone Committee approval -- Final approval by local government -- Imposition of tax.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1406(1): 63N-3-1405(2); 63N-3-1405
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1406(1)(a): 63N-3-1405(2) The legislative body of the local government shall, no later than the date that is 14 calendar days after the date that notice of a proposed project area and proposed participation agreement is provided under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1406(1)(a)(i): endorse the application by:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1406(1)(a)(i)(A): endorsing the proposed project area, with or without amendment; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1406(1)(a)(i)(B): endorsing the proposed participation agreement, with or without amendment; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1406(1)(a)(ii): reject the application.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1406(1)(b): If the legislative body of the local government endorses the application, the legislative body shall provide notice of the endorsement to the Revitalization Zone Committee, and provide the committee with any amended project area or amended participation agreement.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1406(1)(c): 63N-3-1405 If the legislative body of the local government rejects the application:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1406(1)(c)(i): the legislative body shall provide notice of the rejection to the mayor of the local government; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1406(1)(c)(ii): 63N-3-1405 the applicant and the local government may develop another proposed project area and proposed participation agreement and present those documents according to the procedures and requirements of Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1406(2): 63N-3-1405 If the legislative body of the local government endorses the application under Subsection (1):
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1406(2)(a): The Revitalization Zone Committee shall, no later than 30 calendar days after the date that notice of the local government's endorsement of an application is provided under Subsection (1)(b), in a public meeting by a majority vote:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1406(2)(a)(i): approve or reject the endorsed project area; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1406(2)(a)(ii): approve or reject the endorsed project participation agreement.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1406(2)(b): If the committee approves the endorsed project area and the endorsed participation agreement:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1406(2)(b)(i): the committee shall give notice of the approval to the mayor and the legislative body of the local government; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1406(2)(b)(ii): the legislative body of the local government may meet to consider final approval as provided under Subsection (3).
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1406(2)(c): 63N-3-1405 If the committee fails to approve the endorsed project area, the endorsed participation agreement, or both the project area and participation agreement:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1406(2)(c)(i): the committee may adopt a statement or findings as to why the committee failed to provide its approval;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1406(2)(c)(ii): the committee shall give notice of the failure to approve to the mayor and the legislative body of the local government; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1406(2)(c)(iii): 63N-3-1405 the local government may:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1406(2)(c)(iii)(A): 63N-3-1405 develop another proposed project area and proposed participation agreement according to the procedures and requirements of Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1406(2)(c)(iii)(B): in a public meeting of the legislative body of the local government, review, amend, or endorse another project area or participation agreement according to the procedures and requirements of Subsection (1); or
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1406(2)(c)(iii)(C): take no further action on the application.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1406(3): If the Revitalization Zone Committee approves the endorsed project area and the endorsed public participation agreement under Subsection (2), the legislative body of the local government may, by a majority vote in a public meeting:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1406(3)(a): give final approval to the application by:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1406(3)(a)(i): approving the project area in the form approved by the committee;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1406(3)(a)(ii): approving the proposed participation agreement in the form approved by the committee; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1406(3)(a)(iii): designating the applicant as a project participant; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1406(3)(b): reject the application.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1406(4): 59-12-402.5; 63N-3-1408(2) After giving final approval to the application, the local government shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1406(4)(a): 59-12-402.5 impose taxes or revenue sources that may be used within the project area, including taxes or funds authorized under Section
