Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1407 Revitalization Zone Committee -- Creation -- Membership -- Staff.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1407(1): There is created the Revitalization Zone Committee to review the activities of, and advise a local government and project participants in a project area created under this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1407(2): The committee consists of the following members:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1407(2)(a): two members of the Senate, appointed by the president of the Senate;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1407(2)(b): two members of the House of Representatives, appointed by the speaker of the House; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1407(2)(c): one individual appointed by the governor.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1407(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1407(3)(a): The president of the Senate shall designate a member of the Senate appointed under Subsection (2) as cochair of the committee.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1407(3)(b): The speaker of the House of Representatives shall designate a member of the House of Representatives appointed under Subsection (2) as cochair of the committee.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1407(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1407(4)(a): A majority of the members of the committee constitutes a quorum.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1407(4)(b): The action of a majority of a quorum constitutes action of the Revitalization Zone Committee.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1407(5): 63N-3-1406 The committee shall meet to review an endorsed application as provided under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1407(6): 63N-3-1408 The committee may meet, upon the agreement of both cochairs:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1407(6)(a): 63N-3-1408 to review a report provided under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1407(6)(b): at the discretion of the cochairs; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1407(6)(c): at the request of a local government.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1407(7): 36-2-2 A legislative member of the committee shall be paid salary and expenses in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1407(8): 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107; 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107 A member who is not a legislator may not receive compensation or benefits for the member's service, but may receive per diem and travel expenses as allowed in:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1407(8)(a): 63A-3-106 Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1407(8)(b): 63A-3-107 Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1407(8)(c): 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107 rules made by the Division of Finance according to Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1407(9): The Office of Legislative Research and General Counsel shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1407(9)(a): provide staff support to the committee; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1407(9)(b): consult with the Office of the Legislative Fiscal Analyst on fiscal issues reviewed by the committee.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1408 Revitalization Zone Committee -- Duties -- Reporting requirements of local government -- Executive Appropriations Committee.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1408(1): 63N-3-1406 The Revitalization Zone Committee shall have the following duties:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1408(1)(a): 63N-3-1406 to approve or reject an endorsed project area and an endorsed project participation agreement according to the procedures and requirements of Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1408(1)(b): to review reports that are issued by a local government in accordance with Subsection (2);
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1408(1)(c): to review the financial activities of a local government and project participants in relation to a project area; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1408(1)(d): to make recommendations to the Legislature regarding a project area and participation agreement, requirements or procedures related to a project area, taxes or public funds, or other matters relating to a project area or participation agreement.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1408(2): 63N-3-1406 A local government shall, after giving final approval to an application under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1408(2)(a): a summary of the projects and uses that are currently underway or planned in relation to the project area;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1408(2)(b): if not previously provided, or if modified, a copy of the project area and participation agreement;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1408(2)(c): a detailed accounting of:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1408(2)(c)(i): all public funds collected within the project area since the last report;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1408(2)(c)(ii): all public funds provided to each project participant since the last report; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1408(2)(c)(iii): all public funds committed or spent, and a description of their use, since the last report;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1408(2)(d): the projected budget and time line for each project or use that is currently underway or planned in relation to the project area; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1408(2)(e): an accounting or a detailed summary of the financial impact of the project area on the state and its residents.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1408(3): 63N-3-1405; 63N-3-1406 At the discretion of the Executive Appropriations Committee of the Legislature, the local government and the Revitalization Zone Committee shall provide an in-person report to the Executive Appropriations Committee:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1408(3)(a): at least once per calendar year, that shall contain at least the following information:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1408(3)(a)(i): a summary of the projects and uses that are currently underway or planned in relation to the project area;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1408(3)(a)(ii): a detailed accounting of:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1408(3)(a)(ii)(A): all public funds collected within the project area since the last report;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1408(3)(a)(ii)(B): all public funds provided to each project participant since the last report; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1408(3)(a)(ii)(C): all public funds committed or spent, and a description of their use, since the last report;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1408(3)(a)(iii): the projected budget and time line for each project or use that is currently underway or planned in relation to the project area;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1408(3)(a)(iv): an accounting or a detailed summary of the financial impact of the project area on the state and its residents;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1408(3)(a)(v): any recommendations or requests from the local government; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1408(3)(a)(vi): any recommendations or requests form the Revitalization Zone Committee;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1408(3)(b): 63N-3-1405 after the local government provides a proposed project area and proposed participation agreement under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1408(3)(c): 63N-3-1406 after the local government gives final approval to an application under Section

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1501 Definitions.
---------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1501(1): "Business entity" means a for-profit or nonprofit organization.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1501(2): 63N-3-1502 "Pilot program" means the Innovation in Artificial Intelligence Grant Pilot Program created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1501(3): "Student" means a child enrolled in a public or private school, grades kindergarten through twelfth grade.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1502 Innovation in Artificial Intelligence Grant Pilot Program created -- Purpose -- Requirements -- Report.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1502(1): There is created the Innovation in Artificial Intelligence Grant Pilot Program, to be administered subject to the availability of funds by the office as described in this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1502(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1502(2)(a): The purpose of the pilot program is to award a grant to a business entity to develop a program, material, and curriculum to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1502(2)(a)(i): teach a course on artificial intelligence to students, with an emphasis on practical training; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1502(2)(a)(ii): prepare students for career opportunities in technology.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1502(2)(b): A business entity that is awarded a grant under this section shall work in partnership with a public or private school.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1502(3): A business entity that submits an application for a grant to the office shall include the following details in the application:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1502(3)(a): how the business entity proposes to fulfill the purpose described in Subsection (2)(a);
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1502(3)(b): how the business entity proposes to work with a public or private school, as described in Subsection (2)(b); and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1502(3)(c): any existing or planned partnership between the business entity and another individual or business entity to implement the proposal in the application.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1502(4): In evaluating an application for a grant, the office shall consider:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1502(4)(a): the likelihood that the business entity's proposal will accomplish the purpose described in Subsection (2)(a); and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1502(4)(b): the overall viability of the proposal.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1502(5): Before a business entity that has an approved application for a grant may receive grant funds, the business entity shall enter into a written agreement with the office that specifies:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1502(5)(a): the grant amount; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1502(5)(b): the time period and structure for distribution of grant funds, including any terms and conditions the office requires.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1502(6): The office may make rules in accordance with Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act, to administer the pilot program, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1502(6)(a): establishing criteria and procedures for applying for and awarding a grant under this section; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1502(6)(b): reporting requirements from a business entity after a grant is awarded.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1502(7): 63N-1a-306 The office shall include an annual written update on the pilot program in the report described in Section


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1601 Definitions.
---------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1601(1): "Affordable housing" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1601(1)(a): for homes that are not owner occupied, housing occupied or reserved for occupancy by households with a gross household income equal to or less than 80% of the median gross income of the applicable municipal statistical area for households of the same size; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1601(1)(b): for homes that are owner occupied, housing that is priced at 80% of the county median home price.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1601(2): 17C-1-102 "Agency" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1601(3): 63N-3-602 "Base taxable value" means the same as that term is defined in Section

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1601(6): 63N-3-602 "Dwelling unit" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1601(7): "Extraterritorial home" means a dwelling unit that is included as part of the first home investment zone proposal that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1601(7)(a): is located within the municipality proposing the first home investment zone but outside the boundary of the first home investment zone;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1601(7)(b): is part of a development with a density of at least six units per acre;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1601(7)(c): is not located within an existing housing and transit reinvestment zone or an area that could be included in a housing and transit reinvestment zone;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1601(7)(d): has not been issued a building permit by the municipality as of the date of the approval of the first home investment zone; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1601(7)(e): is required to be owner occupied for no less than 25 years.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1601(8): "First home investment zone" means a first home investment zone created in accordance with this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1601(9): "Home" means a dwelling unit.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1601(10): 63N-3-602 "Housing and transit reinvestment zone" means the same as that term is defined in Section

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1601(16)(a): used for a single-family residential purpose; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1601(16)(b): required to be occupied by the owner of the real property for no less than 25 years.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1601(17): 17C-1-102 "Project area" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1601(18): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1601(18)(a): "Project improvements" means site improvements and facilities that are:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1601(18)(a)(i): planned and designed to provide service for development resulting from a development activity;

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1601(21)(a)(i): 59-2-924 the amount of property tax revenue generated each tax year by a taxing entity from the area within a first home investment zone designated in the first home investment zone proposal as the area from which tax increment is to be collected, using the current assessed value and each taxing entity's current certified tax rate as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1601(21)(a)(ii): 59-2-924 the amount of property tax revenue that would be generated from that same area using the base taxable value and each taxing entity's current certified tax rate as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1601(21)(b): 59-2-1602; 59-2-1602 "Tax increment" does not include property tax revenue from:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1601(21)(b)(i): 59-2-1602 a multicounty assessing and collecting levy described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1601(21)(b)(ii): 59-2-1602 a county additional property tax described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1601(22): 17C-1-102 "Taxing entity" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1601(23): "Unencumbered annual community reinvestment agency revenue" means tax increment revenue received by the agency for purposes identified in Title 17C, Limited Purpose Local Government Entities - Community Reinvestment Agency Act, that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1601(23)(a): have not been designated or restricted for future qualified uses as approved by the agency board related to a specific project area; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1601(23)(b): do not have a date certain by which the tax increment revenues will be used.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602 Applicability, requirements, and limitations on a first home investment zone.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(1): 10-9a-403 A first home investment zone created pursuant to this part shall promote the following objectives:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(1)(a): encouraging efficient development and opportunities for home ownership by providing a variety of housing options, including affordable housing and for sale, owner-occupied housing;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(1)(b): improving availability of housing options;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(1)(c): overcoming development impediments and market conditions that render a development cost prohibitive absent the proposal and incentives;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(1)(d): conserving water resources through efficient land use;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(1)(e): improving air quality by reducing fuel consumption and motor vehicle trips;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(1)(f): encouraging transformative mixed-use development;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(1)(g): 10-9a-403 strategic land use and municipal planning in major transit investment corridors as described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(1)(h): increasing access to employment and educational opportunities;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(1)(i): increasing access to child care; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(1)(j): improving efficiencies in parking and transportation, including walkability of communities, street and path interconnectivity within the proposed development and connections to surrounding communities, and access to roadways, public transportation, and active transportation.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(2): In order to accomplish the objectives described in Subsection (1), a municipality or county that initiates the process to create a first home investment zone as described in this part shall ensure that the proposal for a first home investment zone includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(2)(a): subject to Subsection (3), a minimum of 30 housing units per acre in at least 51% of the developable area within the first home investment zone;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(2)(b): a mixed use development;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(2)(c): a requirement that at least 25% of homes within the first home investment zone remain owner occupied for at least 25 years from the date of original purchase;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(2)(d): for homes inside the first home investment zone, a requirement that at least 12% of the owner occupied homes and 12% of the homes that are not owner occupied are affordable housing; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(2)(e): a requirement that at least 20% of the extraterritorial homes are affordable housing.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(3)(a): Subject to Subsection (3)(b), to satisfy the requirements described in Subsection (2)(a), a first home investment zone may include an extraterritorial home to count toward the required density of the first home investment zone by:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(3)(a)(i): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(3)(a)(i)(A): taking the total number of extraterritorial homes related to the first home investment zone; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(3)(a)(i)(B): adding the total number under Subsection (3)(a)(i)(A) to the number of homes within the first home investment zone; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(3)(a)(ii): dividing the total described in Subsection (3)(a)(i) by the total number of developable acres with the first home investment zone.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(3)(b): Extraterritorial homes may account for no more than half of the total homes to calculate density within a first home investment zone.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(4): 63N-3-1605
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(4)(a): If a municipality proposes a first home investment zone, the proposal shall comply with the limitations described in this Subsection (4).
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(4)(b): A first home investment zone may not be less than 10 acres and no more than 100 acres in size.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(4)(c): 63N-3-1605
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(4)(c)(i): Except as provided in Subsection (4)(c)(ii), a first home investment zone is required to be one contiguous area.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(4)(c)(ii): 63N-3-1605 While considering a first home investment zone proposal as described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(4)(c)(ii)(A): the municipality provides evidence in the proposal showing that the deviation from the contiguity requirement will enhance the ability of the first home investment zone to achieve the objectives described in Subsection (1); and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(4)(c)(ii)(B): the housing and transit reinvestment zone committee determines that the deviation is reasonable and circumstances justify deviation from the contiguity requirement.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(4)(c)(iii): The first home investment zone area contiguity is not affected by roads or other rights-of-way.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(4)(d): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(4)(d)(i): A first home investment zone proposal may propose the capture of a maximum of 60% of each taxing entity's tax increment above the base year for a term of no more than 25 consecutive years within a 45-year period not to exceed the tax increment amount approved in the first home investment zone proposal.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(4)(d)(ii): A first home investment zone proposal may not propose or include triggering more than three tax increment collection periods during the applicable 25-year period.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(4)(d)(iii): Subject to Subsection (4)(d)(iv), a municipality shall ensure that the required affordable housing units are included proportionally in each phase of the first home investment zone development.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(4)(d)(iv): A municipality may allow a first home investment zone to be phased and developed in a manner to provide more of the required affordable housing units in early phases of development.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(4)(e): If a municipality proposes a first home investment zone, commencement of the collection of tax increment, for all or a portion of the first home investment zone, is triggered by providing notice as described in Subsection (5).
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(4)(f): A municipality may restrict homes within a first home investment zone and related extraterritorial homes from being used as a short-term rental.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(4)(g): A municipality shall ensure that affordable housing within a first home investment zone and related extraterritorial homes that are reserved as affordable housing are spread throughout the overall development.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(4)(h): A municipality shall ensure that at least 80% of extraterritorial homes included in a first home investment zone proposal are single-family detached homes.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(4)(i): A municipality shall include in a first home investment zone proposal:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(4)(i)(i): an affordable housing plan, which may include deed restrictions, to ensure the affordable housing required in the proposal will continue to meet the definition of affordable housing at least throughout the entire term of the first home investment zone; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(4)(i)(ii): an owner occupancy plan, which may include deed restrictions, to ensure the owner occupancy requirements in the proposal will continue to meet the definition of owner occupancy at least throughout the entire term of the first home investment zone.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(4)(j): A municipality shall include in the first home investment zone proposal evidence to demonstrate how the first home investment zone proposal complies with the municipality's moderate income housing plan and general plan.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(5): Notice of commencement of collection of tax increment shall be sent by mail or electronically to the following entities no later than January 1 of the year for which the tax increment collection is proposed to commence:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(5)(a): the State Tax Commission;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(5)(b): the State Board of Education;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(5)(c): the state auditor;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(5)(d): the auditor of the county in which the first home investment zone is located;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(5)(e): each taxing entity affected by the collection of tax increment from the first home investment zone;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(5)(f): the assessor of the county in which the first home investment zone is located; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(5)(g): the Governor's Office of Economic Opportunity.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(6): A first home investment zone proposal may not include a proposal to capture sales and use tax increment.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(7): 63N-3-603 A municipality may not propose a first home investment zone in a county of the first class if the limitation described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(8): A municipality may not propose a first home investment zone in a location that is eligible for a housing and transit reinvestment zone.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1602(9): A municipality may not propose a first home investment zone if the municipality's community reinvestment agency, based on the most recent annual comprehensive financial report, retains cash and cash equivalent assets of more than 20% of ongoing and unencumbered annual community reinvestment agency revenue.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1603 Process for a proposal of a first home investment zone.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1603(1): 63N-3-1604; 63N-3-1602; 63N-3-1602; 63N-3-1602; 63N-3-1602 Subject to approval of the housing and transit reinvestment zone committee as described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1603(1)(a): 63N-3-1602; 63N-3-1602; 63N-3-1602; 63N-3-1602 prepare a proposal for the first home investment zone that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1603(1)(a)(i): 63N-3-1602 demonstrates that the proposed first home investment zone will meet the objectives described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1603(1)(a)(ii): 63N-3-1602 explains how the municipality will achieve the requirements of Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1603(1)(a)(iii): defines the specific infrastructure needs, if any, and proposed improvements;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1603(1)(a)(iv): demonstrates how the first home investment zone will ensure:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1603(1)(a)(iv)(A): sufficient pedestrian access to schools and other areas of community; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1603(1)(a)(iv)(B): inclusion of child care facilities and access;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1603(1)(a)(v): defines the boundaries of the first home investment zone;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1603(1)(a)(vi): includes maps of the proposed first home investment zone to illustrate:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1603(1)(a)(vi)(A): proposed housing density within the first home investment zone;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1603(1)(a)(vi)(B): extraterritorial homes relevant to the first home investment zone, including density of the development of extraterritorial homes; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1603(1)(a)(vi)(C): existing zoning and proposed zoning changes related to the first home investment zone;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1603(1)(a)(vii): identifies any development impediments that prevent the development from being a market-rate investment and proposed strategies for addressing each one;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1603(1)(a)(viii): 63N-3-1602 describes the proposed development plan, including the requirements described in Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1603(1)(a)(ix): establishes the collection period or periods to calculate the tax increment;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1603(1)(a)(x): describes projected maximum revenues generated and the amount of tax increment capture from each taxing entity and proposed expenditures of revenue derived from the first home investment zone;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1603(1)(a)(xi): includes an analysis of other applicable or eligible incentives, grants, or sources of revenue that can be used to reduce the finance gap;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1603(1)(a)(xii): proposes a finance schedule to align expected revenue with required financing costs and payments;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1603(1)(a)(xiii): evaluates possible benefits to active transportation, public transportation availability and utilization, street connectivity, and air quality; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1603(1)(a)(xiv): 63N-3-1602 provides a pro forma for the planned development that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1603(1)(a)(xiv)(A): 63N-3-1602 satisfies the requirements described in Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1603(1)(a)(xiv)(B): includes data showing the cost difference between what type of development could feasibly be developed absent the first home investment zone tax increment and the type of development that is proposed to be developed with the first home investment zone tax increment;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1603(1)(b): submit the proposal to the relevant school district to discuss the requirements of the proposal and whether the proposal provides the benefits and achieves the objectives described in this part; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1603(1)(c): submit the first home investment zone proposal to the Governor's Office of Economic Opportunity.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1603(2): As part of the proposal described in Subsection (1), a municipality shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1603(2)(a): study and evaluate possible impacts of a proposed first home investment zone on parking and efficient use of land within the municipality and first home investment zone; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1603(2)(b): include in the first home investment zone proposal the findings of the study described in Subsection (2)(a) and proposed strategies to efficiently address parking impacts.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1603(3): 63N-3-1602
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1603(3)(a): After receiving the proposal as described in Subsection (1)(c), the Governor's Office of Economic Opportunity shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1603(3)(a)(i): within 14 days after the date on which the Governor's Office of Economic Opportunity receives the proposal described in Subsection (1)(c), provide notice of the proposal to all affected taxing entities, including the State Tax Commission, cities, counties, school districts, metropolitan planning organizations, and the county assessor and county auditor of the county in which the first home investment zone is located; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1603(3)(a)(ii): at the expense of the proposing municipality as described in Subsection (5), contract with an independent entity to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1603(3)(a)(ii)(A): perform the gap analysis described in Subsection (3)(b); and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1603(3)(a)(ii)(B): perform an analysis of the pro-forma described in Subsection (1)(a)(xiv)(B) and the feasibility of the proposed development absent the tax increment.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1603(3)(b): 63N-3-1602 The gap and pro-forma analysis required in Subsection (3)(a)(ii) shall include:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1603(3)(b)(i): a description of the planned development;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1603(3)(b)(ii): a market analysis relative to other comparable project developments included in or adjacent to the municipality absent the proposed first home investment zone;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1603(3)(b)(iii): an evaluation of the proposal and a determination of the adequacy and efficiency of the proposal;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1603(3)(b)(iv): an evaluation of the proposed tax increment capture needed to cover the system improvements and project improvements associated with the first home investment zone proposal and enable the proposed development to occur, and for the benefit of affordable housing projects; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1603(3)(b)(v): 63N-3-1602 based on the market analysis and other findings, an opinion relative to the appropriate amount of potential public financing reasonably determined to be necessary to achieve the objectives described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1603(3)(c): After receiving notice from the Governor's Office of Economic Opportunity of a proposed first home investment zone as described in Subsection (3)(a)(i), the municipality, in consultation with the county assessor and the State Tax Commission, shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1603(3)(c)(i): evaluate the feasibility of administering the tax implications of the proposal; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1603(3)(c)(ii): provide a letter to the Governor's Office of Economic Opportunity describing any challenges in the administration of the proposal, or indicating that the county assessor can feasibly administer the proposal.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1603(4): After receiving the results from the analysis described in Subsection (3)(b), the municipality proposing the first home investment zone may:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1603(4)(a): amend the first home investment zone proposal based on the findings of the analysis described in Subsection (3)(b) and request that the Governor's Office of Economic Opportunity submit the amended first home investment zone proposal to the housing and transit reinvestment zone committee; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1603(4)(b): request that the Governor's Office of Economic Opportunity submit the original first home investment zone proposal to the housing and transit reinvestment zone committee.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1603(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1603(5)(a): The Governor's Office of Economic Opportunity may accept, as a dedicated credit, up to $20,000 from a municipality for the costs of the gap analysis described in Subsection (3)(b).
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1603(5)(b): The Governor's Office of Economic Opportunity may expend funds received from a municipality as dedicated credits to pay for the costs associated with the gap analysis described in Subsection (3)(b).

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1608 Tax increment protections.
-----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1608(1): 63N-3-1606 Upon petition by a participating taxing entity or on the initiative of the housing and transit reinvestment zone committee creating a first home investment zone, a first home investment zone may suspend or terminate the collection of tax increment in a first home investment zone if the housing and transit reinvestment zone committee determines, by clear and convincing evidence, presented in a public meeting of the housing and transit reinvestment zone committee, that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1608(1)(a): 63N-3-1606 a substantial portion of the tax increment collected in the first home investment zone has not or will not be used for the purposes provided in Section

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-3-1609 Boundary adjustments.
------------------------------------------------------
If the relevant county assessor or county auditor adjusts parcel boundaries relevant to a first home investment zone, the municipality administering the tax increment collected in the first home investment zone may make corresponding adjustments to the boundary of the first home investment zone.

Utah Code Annotated - Title 63N - Chapter 4 - Rural Development Act
*******************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-101 Title -- Definitions.
-----------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-101(1): This chapter is known as the "Rural Development Act."
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-101(2): 63N-4-102 As used in this part, "program" means the Rural Development Program created in Section


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-102 Rural Development Program -- Supervision by office.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-102(1): There is created within the office the Center for Rural Development.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-102(2): The Center for Rural Development is under the administration and general supervision of the office.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-103 Purpose of the Center for Rural Development.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------
The Center for Rural Development is established to:Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-103(1): foster and support economic development programs and activities for the benefit of rural counties and communities;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-103(2): foster and support community, county, and resource management planning programs and activities for the benefit of rural counties and communities;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-103(3): foster and support leadership training programs and activities for the benefit of:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-103(3)(a): rural leaders in both the public and private sectors;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-103(3)(b): economic development and planning personnel; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-103(3)(c): rural government officials;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-103(4): foster and support efforts to coordinate and focus the technical and other resources of appropriate institutions of higher education, local governments, private sector interests, associations, nonprofit organizations, federal agencies, and others, in ways that address the economic development, planning, and leadership challenges;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-103(5): work to enhance the capacity of GOEO to address rural economic development, planning, and leadership training challenges and opportunities by establishing partnerships and positive working relationships with appropriate public and private sector entities, individuals, and institutions; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-103(6): foster government-to-government collaboration and good working relations between state and rural government regarding economic development and planning issues.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-104 Duties.
---------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-104(1): 63N-4-802 The Center for Rural Development shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-104(1)(a): work to enhance the capacity of the office to address rural economic development, planning, and leadership training challenges and opportunities by establishing partnerships and positive working relationships with appropriate public and private sector entities, individuals, and institutions;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-104(1)(b): work with the GOEO board to coordinate and focus available resources in ways that address the economic development, planning, and leadership training challenges and priorities in rural Utah;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-104(1)(c): 63N-4-802 assist in administering the Rural Opportunity Program created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-104(1)(d): in accordance with economic development and planning policies set by state government, coordinate relations between:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-104(1)(d)(i): the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-104(1)(d)(ii): rural governments;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-104(1)(d)(iii): other public and private groups engaged in rural economic planning and development; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-104(1)(d)(iv): federal agencies.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-104(2): The Center for Rural Development may, in accordance with Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act, make rules necessary to carry out its duties.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-105 Program manager.
------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-105(1): The executive director may appoint a director for the Center for Rural Development with the approval of the governor.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-105(2): The director of the Center for Rural Development shall be a person knowledgeable in the field of rural economic development and planning and experienced in administration.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-105(3): Upon change of the executive director, the director of the Center for Rural Development may not be dismissed without cause for at least 180 days.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-106 Annual report.
----------------------------------------------
The office shall include in the annual written report described in Section

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-306 Request for determination.
----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-306(1): A rural investment company, before making a growth investment, may request from the office a written opinion as to whether the business in which a rural investment company proposes to invest is an eligible small business.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-306(2): The office shall notify the rural investment company of the office's determination within 30 days after receipt of the request.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-306(3): If the office fails to notify the rural investment company of the office's determination in accordance with this section, the business in which the rural investment company proposes to invest shall be considered an eligible small business.

-------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-308(1): The office shall calculate an annual fee to be paid by each rural investment company by dividing $50,000 by the number of rural investment companies approved under this part and notify each rural investment company of the amount of the annual fee.

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-401 Title.
--------------------------------------
This part is known as the "Rural Employment Expansion Program."

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-402 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-402(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-402(1)(a): "Business entity" means a sole proprietorship, partnership, association, joint venture, corporation, firm, trust, foundation, or other organization or entity used in carrying on a business.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-402(1)(b): "Business entity" does not include a business primarily engaged in the following:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-402(1)(b)(i): construction;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-402(1)(b)(ii): staffing;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-402(1)(b)(iii): retail trade; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-402(1)(b)(iv): public utility activities.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-402(2): 63N-4-403 "Grant" means a grant awarded as part of the Rural Employment Expansion Grant Program created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-402(3): 63N-4-403 "Grant program" means the Rural Employment Expansion Grant Program created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-402(4): "Mining company" means an entity whose primary business is the exploration for or extraction of minerals from the earth.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-402(5): "Mining services company" means an entity whose primary business is providing support services for a mining company, including drilling or geological modeling.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-402(6): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-402(6)(a): "Owner or officer" means an individual who owns an ownership interest in an entity or holds a position where the person has authority to manage, direct, control, or make decisions for:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-402(6)(a)(i): the entity or a portion of the entity; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-402(6)(a)(ii): an employee, agent, or independent contractor of the entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-402(6)(b): "Owner or officer" includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-402(6)(b)(i): a member of a board of directors or other governing body of an entity; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-402(6)(b)(ii): a partner in any type of partnership.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-402(7): "Rural county" means a county of the third, fourth, fifth, or sixth class.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-403 Creation of Rural Employment Expansion Grant Program -- Duties of the office.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-403(1): There is created the Rural Employment Expansion Grant Program administered by the office.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-403(2): 63N-1a-306 The office shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-403(2)(a): review a business entity's application for a grant in the order in which the application is received by the office;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-403(2)(b): ensure that a grant is only awarded to a business entity that meets the requirements of this part; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-403(2)(c): 63N-1a-306 as part of the annual written report described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-403(2)(c)(i): the identity of each business entity that was provided a grant by the office during the year of the annual report;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-403(2)(c)(ii): the total amount awarded in grants for each county; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-403(2)(c)(iii): an evaluation of the effectiveness of the grant in bringing significant new employment to rural communities.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-403(3): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act The office may:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-403(3)(a): authorize a grant for a business entity under this part;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-403(3)(b): audit a business entity to ensure:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-403(3)(b)(i): eligibility for a grant; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-403(3)(b)(ii): compliance with this part; and

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-403(3)(c)(iii): administration of grants, including an appeal process and relevant timelines and deadlines.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-404 Grant application process.
----------------------------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-404(4)(a)(i): $4,000 for each new full-time employee position in a county where the average county wage is equal to or greater than the state average wage;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-404(4)(a)(ii): $5,000 for each new full-time employee position in a county where the average county wage is between 85% and 99% of the state average wage; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-404(4)(a)(iii): $6,000 for each new full-time employee position in a county where the average county wage is less than 85% of the state average wage.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-404(4)(b): A business entity may qualify for no more than $250,000 in grants in any fiscal year.

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-501 Title.
--------------------------------------
This part is known as the "Rural Coworking and Innovation Center Grant Program."

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-502 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-502(1): "Coworking and innovation center" means a facility designed to provide individuals with the infrastructure and equipment to participate in the online workforce.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-502(2): "Entity" means a county, city, nonprofit organization, or institution of higher education.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-502(3): 63N-4-503 "Grant" means a grant awarded as part of the Rural Coworking and Innovation Center Grant Program created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-502(4): 63N-4-503 "Grant program" means the Rural Coworking and Innovation Center Grant Program created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-502(5): "Rural area" means any area in any county in the state except Salt Lake, Utah, Davis, Weber, Washington, Cache, Tooele, and Summit counties.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-503 Creation and purpose of the Rural Coworking and Innovation Center Grant Program.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-503(1): There is created the Rural Coworking and Innovation Center Grant Program administered by the office.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-503(2): The office may seek to accomplish the following objectives in administering the grant program:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-503(2)(a): constructing or renovating a facility in one or more rural areas to create one or more coworking and innovation centers;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-503(2)(b): extending and improving utilities and broadband service connections to one or more coworking and innovation centers in one or more rural areas; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-503(2)(c): purchasing equipment, furniture, and security systems as part of one or more coworking and innovation centers in one or more rural areas.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-504 Requirements for awarding a working hubs grant.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-504(1): In accordance with Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act, the office shall make rules establishing the eligibility and reporting criteria for an entity to receive a grant under this part, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-504(1)(a): the form and process of submitting an application to the office for a grant;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-504(1)(b): which entities are eligible to apply for a grant;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-504(1)(c): the method and formula for determining grant amounts; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-504(1)(d): the reporting requirements of grant recipients.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-504(2): In determining the award of a grant, the office may prioritize projects:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-504(2)(a): that will serve underprivileged or underserved communities, including communities with high unemployment or low median incomes;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-504(2)(b): where an applicant demonstrates comprehensive planning of the project but has limited access to financial resources, including financial resources from local or county government; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-504(2)(c): that maximize economic development opportunities in collaboration with the economic development needs or plans of an educational institution, a county, and a municipality.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-504(3): Subject to legislative appropriation, a grant may only be awarded by the executive director.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-504(4): A grant may only be awarded under this part:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-504(4)(a): if the grant recipient agrees to provide any combination of funds, land, buildings, or in-kind work in an amount equal to at least 25% of the grant;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-504(4)(b): if the grant recipient agrees not to use grant money for the ongoing operation or maintenance of a coworking and innovation center; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-504(4)(c): in an amount no more than $500,000 to a grant applicant.

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-801(11)(b): a county of the second class, if the municipality has a population of 10,000 or less.

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-802 Creation of Rural Opportunity Program -- Awarding of grants and loans -- Rulemaking -- Reporting.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-802(1): There is created the Rural Opportunity Program.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-802(2): The program shall be overseen by the advisory committee and administered by the office.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-802(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-802(3)(a): In overseeing the program, the advisory committee shall make recommendations to the office on the awarding of grants and loans under this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-802(3)(b): After reviewing the recommendations of the advisory committee, and subject to appropriations from the Legislature, the office shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-802(3)(b)(i): award grants to rural communities and business entities in accordance with Subsection (4) and rules made by the center under Subsection (6); and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-802(3)(b)(ii): award loans to rural communities in accordance with Subsection (5) and rules made by the center under Subsection (6).
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-802(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-802(4)(a): The office shall annually distribute an equal amount of grant money to all rural counties that have created a CEO board and apply for a grant, in an amount up to and including $200,000 annually per county.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-802(4)(b): In addition to the grant money distributed to rural counties under Subsection (4)(a), the office may use program funds to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-802(4)(b)(i): award grants to rural communities that demonstrate a funding match, in an amount established by rule under Subsection (6);
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-802(4)(b)(ii): award grants to business entities that create new jobs within rural communities;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-802(4)(b)(iii): award grants to associations of governments, subject to Subsection (4)(e); and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-802(4)(b)(iv): award grants to rural health care special districts.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-802(4)(c): The office shall award grants under this Subsection (4) to address the economic development needs of rural communities, which needs may include:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-802(4)(c)(i): business recruitment, development, and expansion;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-802(4)(c)(ii): workforce training and development; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-802(4)(c)(iii): infrastructure, industrial building development, and capital facilities improvements for business development.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-802(4)(d): In awarding grants under this Subsection (4), the office:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-802(4)(d)(i): shall prioritize applications in accordance with rules made by the office under Subsection (6); and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-802(4)(d)(ii): may not award more than 20% of the total amount of grant funds made available each year to associations of governments.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-802(4)(e): An association of governments may not receive a grant from the program unless the association of governments demonstrates to the office that each county belonging to the association of governments has approved the request for grant funds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-802(5): 11-14-316; 63B-1b-202
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-802(5)(a): In addition to the awarding of grants under Subsection (4), the office may use program funds to award loans to rural communities or rural health care special districts to provide financing for qualified projects.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-802(5)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-802(5)(b)(i): A rural community or rural health care special district may not receive a loan from the program for a qualified project unless:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-802(5)(b)(i)(A): the rural community or rural health care special district demonstrates to the office that the rural community or rural health care special district has exhausted all other means of securing funding from the state for the qualified project; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-802(5)(b)(i)(B): the rural community or rural health care special district enters into a loan contract with the office.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-802(5)(b)(ii): A loan contract under Subsection (5)(b)(i)(B):
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-802(5)(b)(ii)(A): shall be secured by legally issued bonds, notes, or other evidence of indebtedness validly issued under state law, including pledging all or any portion of a revenue source controlled by the rural community or rural health care special district to the repayment of the loan; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-802(5)(b)(ii)(B): may provide that a portion of the proceeds of the loan may be applied to fund a reserve fund to secure the repayment of the loan.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-802(5)(c): A loan under this Subsection (5) shall bear interest as set by the office in consultation with the state treasurer.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-802(5)(d): 11-14-316 Before a rural community or rural health care special district may receive a loan from the office, the rural community or rural health care special district shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-802(5)(d)(i): 11-14-316 publish the rural community's or rural health care special district's intention to obtain the loan at least once in accordance with the publication and notice requirements described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-802(5)(d)(ii): adopt an ordinance or resolution authorizing the loan.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-802(5)(e): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-802(5)(e)(i): If a rural community or rural health care district that receives a loan from the office fails to comply with the terms of the loan contract, the office may seek any legal or equitable remedy to obtain compliance or payment of damages.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-802(5)(e)(ii): If a rural community or rural health care district fails to make loan payments when due, the state shall, at the request of the office, withhold an amount of money due to the rural community or rural health care district and deposit the withheld money into the fund to pay the amount due under the contract.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-802(5)(e)(iii): The office may elect when to take any action or request the withholding of money under this Subsection (5)(e).
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-802(5)(f): 63B-1b-202 All loan contracts, bonds, notes, or other evidence of indebtedness securing any loans shall be collected and accounted for in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-802(6): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-802(6)(a): In accordance with Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act, and in collaboration with the advisory committee, the office shall make rules to administer the program.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-4-802(6)(b): The rules under Subsection (6)(a) shall establish:

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-6-303 Board of directors.
---------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-6-303(1): The corporation's board of directors comprises the state treasurer and two individuals designated by the state treasurer.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-6-303(2): Two members of the board are a quorum for the transaction of business.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-6-303(3): Members of the board of directors:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-6-303(3)(a): are subject to any restrictions on conflicts of interest specified in the organizational documents of the corporation; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-6-303(3)(b): may not participate in a vote by the board of directors related to an investment by the Utah fund of funds, if the member has an interest in the investment.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-6-303(4): Directors of the corporation:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-6-303(4)(a): shall be compensated for direct expenses and mileage; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-6-303(4)(b): may not receive a director's fee or salary for service as directors.

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-6-305(1): The corporation may charge a management fee on assets under management in the Utah fund of funds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-6-305(2): (1) The management fee described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-6-305(3): In addition to the management fee, the Utah fund of funds will pay directly or reimburse the corporation for out-of-pocket expenses, including fund administration, tax and audit fees and costs, investment and monitoring costs, and similar expenses incurred in connection with the operation of the corporation or the Utah fund of funds.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-6-401 Organization of Utah fund of funds.
-------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-6-401(1): The corporation shall organize, and be the sole member and manager of, the Utah fund of funds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-6-401(2): The Utah fund of funds shall hold and manage investments made by the Utah fund of funds and proceeds from those investments until disbursed to the restricted account or used to pay the fees and expenses described in this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-6-401(3): The Utah fund of funds shall be organized as a limited liability company, with the corporation as the sole member and manager.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-6-401(4): The Utah fund of funds may not invest money after May 4, 2022, unless the Utah fund of funds committed to the investment before May 4, 2022.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-6-401(5): The corporation may disburse proceeds of investments from the Utah fund of funds into the restricted account at any time the corporation determines is in the best interest of the state, leaving sufficient funds to pay expenses and fees owed by, or needed to wind up the affairs of, the corporation or the Utah fund of funds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-6-401(6): The state treasurer shall notify the Executive Appropriations Committee when all investments held by the Utah fund of funds mature and the state treasurer determines it is advisable to complete winding up the affairs of the corporation.

Utah Code Annotated - Title 63N - Chapter 7 - Utah Office of Tourism

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-7-101 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 63N-7-101(1): 63N-7-201 "Board" means the Board of Tourism Development created in Section

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-7-101(3): "Sports organization" means an organization that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-7-101(3)(a): is exempt from federal income taxation in accordance with Section 501(c)(3), Internal Revenue Code;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-7-101(3)(b): maintains the organization's principal location in the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-7-101(3)(c): has a minimum of 15 years experience in the state hosting, fostering, and attracting major summer and winter sporting events statewide; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-7-101(3)(d): was created to foster state, regional, national, and international sports competitions in the state, to drive the state's Olympic and sports legacy, including competitions related to Olympic sports, and to promote and encourage sports tourism throughout the state, including advertising, marketing, branding, and promoting the state for the purpose of attracting sporting events in the state.

----------------------------------------------------------------------------
The tourism office may enter into agreements with state or federal agencies to accept services, quarters, or facilities as a contribution in carrying out the duties and functions of the tourism office.

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-7-201 Board of Tourism created -- Members -- Meetings -- Expenses.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-7-201(1): There is created within the tourism office the Board of Tourism Development.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-7-201(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-7-201(2)(a): The board shall consist of 15 members appointed or reappointed by the governor to four-year terms with the advice and consent of the Senate.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-7-201(2)(b): Notwithstanding the requirements of Subsection (2)(a), the governor shall, at the time of appointment or reappointment, adjust the length of terms to ensure that the terms of board members are staggered so that approximately half of the board is appointed every two years.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-7-201(3): The members may not serve more than two full consecutive terms unless the governor determines that an additional term is in the best interest of the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-7-201(4): Not more than eight members of the board may be from the same political party.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-7-201(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-7-201(5)(a): The members shall be representative of:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-7-201(5)(a)(i): all areas of the state with six being appointed from separate geographical areas as provided in Subsection (5)(b); and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-7-201(5)(a)(ii): a diverse mix of business ownership or executive management of tourism related industries.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-7-201(5)(b): The geographical representatives shall be appointed as follows:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-7-201(5)(b)(i): one member from Salt Lake, Tooele, or Morgan County;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-7-201(5)(b)(ii): one member from Davis, Weber, Box Elder, Cache, or Rich County;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-7-201(5)(b)(iii): one member from Utah, Summit, Juab, or Wasatch County;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-7-201(5)(b)(iv): one member from Carbon, Emery, Grand, Duchesne, Daggett, or Uintah County;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-7-201(5)(b)(v): one member from San Juan, Piute, Wayne, Garfield, or Kane County; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-7-201(5)(b)(vi): one member from Washington, Iron, Beaver, Sanpete, Sevier, or Millard County.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-7-201(5)(c): The tourism industry representatives of ownership or executive management shall be appointed as follows:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-7-201(5)(c)(i): one member from ownership or executive management of the lodging industry, as recommended by the tourism industry for the governor's consideration;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-7-201(5)(c)(ii): one member from ownership or executive management of the restaurant industry, as recommended by the restaurant industry for the governor's consideration;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-7-201(5)(c)(iii): one member from ownership or executive management of the ski industry, as recommended by the ski industry for the governor's consideration; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-7-201(5)(c)(iv): one member from ownership or executive management of a tourism-related transportation provider, as recommended by the tourism industry for the governor's consideration.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-7-201(5)(d): One member shall be appointed at large from ownership or executive management of business, finance, economic policy, or the academic media marketing community.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-7-201(5)(e): One member shall be appointed from the Utah Tourism Industry Association, as recommended by the association for the governor's consideration.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-7-201(5)(f): One member shall be appointed to represent the state's counties, as recommended by the Utah Association of Counties for the governor's consideration.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-7-201(5)(g): One member shall be appointed from an arts and cultural organization, as recommended by the arts and cultural community for the governor's consideration.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-7-201(5)(h): One member shall be appointed to represent the outdoor recreation industry, as recommended by the outdoor recreation industry for the governor's consideration.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-7-201(5)(i): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-7-201(5)(i)(i): The governor may choose to disregard a recommendation made for the board members described in Subsections (5)(c), (e), and (f) through (h).
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-7-201(5)(i)(ii): The governor shall request additional recommendations if recommendations are disregarded under Subsection (5)(i)(i).
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-7-201(6): When a vacancy occurs in the membership for any reason, the governor shall, with the advice and consent of the Senate, appoint a replacement for the unexpired term from the same geographic area or industry representation as the member whose office was vacated.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-7-201(7): Eight members of the board constitute a quorum for conducting board business and exercising board powers.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-7-201(8): The governor shall select one of the board members as chair and one of the board members as vice chair, each for a four-year term as recommended by the board for the governor's consideration.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-7-201(9): 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107; 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107 A member may not receive compensation or benefits for the member's service, but may receive per diem and travel expenses in accordance with:

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-7-201(10): The board shall meet monthly or as often as the board determines to be necessary at various locations throughout the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-7-201(11): Members who may have a potential conflict of interest in consideration of fund allocation decisions shall identify the potential conflict prior to voting on the issue.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-7-201(12): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-7-201(12)(a): The board shall determine attendance requirements for maintaining a designated board seat.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-7-201(12)(b): If a board member fails to attend according to the requirements established pursuant to Subsection (12)(a), the board member shall be replaced upon written certification from the board chair or vice chair to the governor.

Utah Code Annotated - Title 63N - Chapter 8 - Motion Picture Incentives
***********************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-101 Title -- Purpose.
-------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-101(1): This chapter is known as "Motion Picture Incentives."
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-101(2): The Legislature finds that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-101(2)(a): the state's natural beauty, scenic wonders, and diverse topography provide a variety of magnificent settings from which the motion picture industry can choose to film part or all of major or independent motion pictures, made-for-television movies, and television series;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-101(2)(b): the state has an abundance of resources, including a skilled and able workforce, the required infrastructure, and a friendly and hospitable populace that have been instrumental in the filming of hundreds of successful motion pictures and several television series; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-101(2)(c): further development of the motion picture industry in Utah is a state public purpose that will significantly impact growth in the state's economy and contribute to the fiscal well being of the state and its people.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-101(3): The purpose of this chapter is to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-101(3)(a): encourage the use of Utah as a site for the production of motion pictures, television series, and made-for-television movies;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-101(3)(b): provide financial incentives to the film industry so that Utah might compete successfully with other states and countries for filming locations; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-101(3)(c): help develop a strong motion picture industry presence in the state that will contribute substantially to improving the state's economy.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-102 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-102(1): "Digital media company" means a company engaged in the production of a digital media project.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-102(2): "Digital media project" means all or part of a production of interactive entertainment or animated production that is produced for distribution in commercial or educational markets, which shall include projects intended for Internet or wireless distribution.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-102(3): 59-10-402 "Dollars left in the state" means expenditures made in the state for a state-approved production, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-102(3)(a): an expenditure that is subject to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-102(3)(a)(i): a corporate franchise or income tax under Title 59, Chapter 7, Corporate Franchise and Income Taxes;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-102(3)(a)(ii): an individual income tax under Title 59, Chapter 10, Individual Income Tax Act;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-102(3)(a)(iii): a sales and use tax under Title 59, Chapter 12, Sales and Use Tax Act, notwithstanding any sales and use tax exemption allowed by law; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-102(3)(a)(iv): a combination of Subsections (3)(a)(i), (ii), and (iii);
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-102(3)(b): payments made to a nonresident only to the extent of the income tax paid to the state on the payments, the amount of per diems paid in the state, and other direct reimbursements transacted in the state; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-102(3)(c): 59-10-402 payments made to a payroll company or loan-out corporation that is registered to do business in the state, only to the extent of the amount of withholding under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-102(4): "Loan-out corporation" means a corporation owned by one or more artists that provides services of the artists to a third party production company.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-102(5): "Motion picture company" means a company engaged in the production of:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-102(5)(a): motion pictures;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-102(5)(b): television series; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-102(5)(c): made-for-television movies.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-102(6): 59-7-614.5; 59-10-1108 "Motion picture incentive" means either a cash rebate from the Motion Picture Incentive Account or a refundable tax credit under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-102(7): "New state revenue" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-102(7)(a): incremental new state sales and use tax revenue generated as a result of a digital media project that a digital media company pays under Title 59, Chapter 12, Sales and Use Tax Act;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-102(7)(b): incremental new state tax revenue that a digital media company pays as a result of a digital media project under:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-102(7)(b)(i): Title 59, Chapter 7, Corporate Franchise and Income Taxes;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-102(7)(b)(ii): Title 59, Chapter 10, Part 1, Determination and Reporting of Tax Liability and Information;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-102(7)(b)(iii): Title 59, Chapter 10, Part 2, Trusts and Estates;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-102(7)(b)(iv): Title 59, Chapter 10, Part 4, Withholding of Tax; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-102(7)(b)(v): a combination of Subsections (7)(b)(i), (ii), (iii), and (iv);
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-102(7)(c): incremental new state revenue generated as individual income taxes under Title 59, Chapter 10, Part 1, Determination and Reporting of Tax Liability and Information, paid by employees of the new digital media project as evidenced by payroll records from the digital media company; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-102(7)(d): a combination of Subsections (7)(a), (b), and (c).
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-102(8): "Payroll company" means a business entity that handles the payroll and becomes the employer of record for the staff, cast, and crew of a motion picture production.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-102(9): 63N-8-103; 59-7-614.5; 59-10-1108 "Refundable tax credit" means a refundable motion picture tax credit authorized under Section

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-104 Motion picture incentives -- Standards to qualify for an incentive -- Limitations -- Content of agreement between office and motion picture company or digital media company.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-104(1): In addition to the requirements for receiving a motion picture incentive as set forth in this part, the office, in accordance with Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act, shall make rules establishing:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-104(1)(a): the standards that a motion picture company or digital media company must meet to qualify for the motion picture incentive; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-104(1)(b): criteria for determining the amount of the incentive.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-104(2): The office shall ensure that those standards include the following:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-104(2)(a): an incentive may only be issued for a state-approved production by a motion picture company or digital media company;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-104(2)(b): financing has been obtained and is in place for the production; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-104(2)(c): the economic impact of the production on the state represents new incremental economic activity in the state as opposed to existing economic activity.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-104(3): With respect to a digital media project, the office shall consider economic modeling, including the costs and benefits of the digital media project to state and local governments in determining the motion picture incentive amount.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-104(4): The office may also consider giving preference to a production that stimulates economic activity in rural areas of the state or that has Utah content, such as recognizing that the production was made in the state or uses Utah as Utah in the production.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-104(5): 63N-7-201; 63N-8-103
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-104(5)(a): 63N-7-201 The office, with advice from the Board of Tourism Development created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-104(5)(b): 63N-8-103 Subject to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-104(5)(b)(i): to a motion picture company of up to 20% of the dollars left in the state by the motion picture company, and a motion picture company can receive an additional 5%, not to exceed 25% of the dollars left in the state by the motion picture company if the company fulfills certain requirements determined by the office including:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-104(5)(b)(i)(A): employing a significant percentage of cast and crew from Utah;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-104(5)(b)(i)(B): highlighting the state of Utah and the Utah Film Commission in the motion picture credits; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-104(5)(b)(i)(C): other promotion opportunities as agreed upon by the office and the motion picture company; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-104(5)(b)(ii): to a digital media company, if the incentive does not exceed 100% of the new state revenue less the considerations under Subsection (3), but not to exceed 20% of the dollars left in the state by the digital media company.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-104(5)(c): The office may not give a cash rebate incentive from the Motion Picture Incentive Restricted Account for a digital media project.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-104(6): The office shall ensure that the agreement entered into with a motion picture company or digital media company under Subsection (5)(a):
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-104(6)(a): details the requirements that the motion picture company or digital media company must meet to qualify for an incentive under this part;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-104(6)(b): specifies:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-104(6)(b)(i): the nature of the incentive; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-104(6)(b)(ii): the maximum amount of the motion picture incentive that the motion picture company or digital media company may earn for a taxable year and over the life of the production;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-104(6)(c): establishes the length of time over which the motion picture company or digital media company may claim the motion picture incentive;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-104(6)(d): requires the motion picture company or digital media company to retain records supporting its claim for a motion picture incentive for at least four years after the motion picture company or digital media company claims the incentive under this part; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-8-104(6)(e): requires the motion picture company or digital media company to submit to audits for verification of the claimed motion picture incentive.
