Utah Code Annotated - Title 63N - Chapter 13 - Procurement Programs
*******************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-101 Title -- Projects to assist companies to secure new business with federal, state, and local governments.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-101(1): This chapter is known as "Procurement Programs."
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-101(2): The Legislature recognizes that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-101(2)(a): many Utah companies provide products and services which are routinely procured by a myriad of governmental entities at all levels of government, but that attempting to understand and comply with the numerous certification, registration, proposal, and contract requirements associated with government procurement often raises significant barriers for those companies with no government contracting experience;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-101(2)(b): the costs associated with obtaining a government contract for products or services often prevent most small businesses from working in the governmental procurement market;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-101(2)(c): currently a majority of federal procurement opportunities are contracted to businesses located outside of the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-101(2)(d): the office currently administers programs and initiatives that help create and grow companies in Utah and recruit companies to Utah through the use of state employees, public-private partnerships, and contractual services; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-101(2)(e): there exists a significant opportunity for Utah companies to secure new business with federal, state, and local governments.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-101(3): The office, through its executive director:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-101(3)(a): shall manage and direct the administration of state and federal programs and initiatives whose purpose is to procure federal, state, and local governmental contracts;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-101(3)(b): may require program accountability measures; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-101(3)(c): may receive and distribute legislative appropriations and public and private grants for projects and programs that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-101(3)(c)(i): are focused on growing Utah companies and positively impacting statewide revenues by helping these companies secure new business with federal, state, and local governments;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-101(3)(c)(ii): provide guidance to Utah companies interested in obtaining new business with federal, state, and local governmental entities;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-101(3)(c)(iii): would facilitate marketing, business development, and expansion opportunities for Utah companies in cooperation with the office's APEX accelerator program and with public, nonprofit, or private sector partners such as local chambers of commerce, trade associations, or private contractors as determined by the office's director to successfully match Utah businesses with government procurement opportunities; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-101(3)(c)(iv): may include the following components:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-101(3)(c)(iv)(A): recruitment, individualized consultation, and an introduction to government contracting;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-101(3)(c)(iv)(B): specialized contractor training for companies located in Utah;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-101(3)(c)(iv)(C): a Utah contractor matching program for government requirements;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-101(3)(c)(iv)(D): experienced proposal and bid support; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-101(3)(c)(iv)(E): specialized support services.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-101(4): (3)
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-101(4)(a): (3) The office, through its executive director, shall make any distribution referred to in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-101(4)(b): A recipient of money distributed under this section shall provide the office with a set of standard monthly reports, the content of which shall be determined by the office to include at least the following information:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-101(4)(b)(i): consultive meetings with Utah companies;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-101(4)(b)(ii): seminars or training meetings held;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-101(4)(b)(iii): government contracts awarded to Utah companies;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-101(4)(b)(iv): increased revenues generated by Utah companies from new government contracts;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-101(4)(b)(v): jobs created;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-101(4)(b)(vi): salary ranges of new jobs; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-101(4)(b)(vii): the value of contracts generated.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-301 Title.
---------------------------------------
This part is known as the "Facilitating Public-Private Partnerships Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-302 Definitions.
---------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-302(1): 63C-25-101 "Bonding government entity" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-302(2): 63C-25-101 "Concessionaire contract" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-302(3): 63N-13-304; 63N-13-304 "Facilitator" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-302(3)(a): 63N-13-304 the office, if the office chooses to perform itself the functions and responsibilities described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-302(3)(b): 63N-13-304 a person engaged by the office to perform the functions and responsibilities described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-302(4): "Government entity" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-302(4)(a): the state or any department, division, agency, or other instrumentality of the state; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-302(4)(b): a political subdivision of the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-302(5): "Public-private partnership" means an arrangement or agreement between a government entity and one or more private persons to fund and provide for a public need through the development or operation of a public project in which the private person or persons share with the government entity the responsibility or risk of developing, owning, maintaining, financing, or operating the project.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-303 Contract with facilitator.
-----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-303(1): 63N-13-304; Title 63G, Chapter 6a, Utah Procurement Code If the office chooses to have the functions and responsibilities described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-303(2): 63H-1-202(9) Except as provided in Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-304 Functions and responsibilities of facilitator.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-304(1): A facilitator shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-304(1)(a): be a single point of contact and information on public-private partnerships in the state for:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-304(1)(a)(i): government entities exploring the possibility of filling a public need through a public-private partnership; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-304(1)(a)(ii): private persons exploring investment opportunities in a public project in the state through a public-private partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-304(1)(b): work throughout the state to identify government entities that may have an interest in seeking to fill a public need through a public-private partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-304(1)(c): work to identify private persons who may have an interest in investment opportunities in public projects in the state through a public-private partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-304(1)(d): facilitate the matching of government entities seeking to fill a public need through a public-private partnership with private persons seeking investment opportunities in public projects through a public-private partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-304(1)(e): facilitate and assist with the establishment of public-private partnerships for government entities who request the facilitator's assistance in establishing a public-private partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-304(1)(f): provide a website with information:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-304(1)(f)(i): about the process for pursuing, developing, and implementing a public-private partnership in the state; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-304(1)(f)(ii): to help government entities and persons seeking investment opportunities through public-private partnerships in the state to understand available public-private partnership opportunities; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-304(1)(g): through promotional, informational, and other activities, work to help move the state to the forefront throughout the country in the area of private participation in public infrastructure development through public-private partnerships.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-304(2): (1); (1) If the office chooses to have the functions and responsibilities described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-304(3): The office may make recommendations for the Legislature to consider relating to public-private partnerships:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-304(3)(a): to enhance the statutory framework for the establishment of public-private partnerships for public infrastructure projects; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-304(3)(b): with the goal of moving the state to the forefront throughout the country in the area of private participation in public infrastructure development through public-private partnerships.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-305 Office oversight over contract performance of facilitator -- Office reports to Legislature.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-305(1): 63N-13-303; 63N-13-304 The office shall monitor and oversee a facilitator's performance under a contract under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-305(2): Before October 1 of each year, the office shall provide an annual report to the Economic Development and Workforce Services Interim Committee of the facilitator's activities under this part.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-306 Limits on application of this part -- Concessionaire contract.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-306(1): Nothing in this part:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-306(1)(a): requires a government entity to use the facilitator to explore the possibility of filling a public need through a public-private partnership; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-306(1)(b): limits the ability of a government entity to directly:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-306(1)(b)(i): solicit a public-private partnership; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-306(1)(b)(ii): respond to a private person exploring an investment opportunity in a public project through a public-private partnership.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-306(2): 63C-25-202 A facilitator shall inform a bonding government entity that is contemplating entering into a concessionaire contract that the bonding government entity may not enter into the concessionaire contract unless the bonding government entity first receives approval from the State Finance Review Commission in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-306(3): A government entity anticipating the possibility of entering into a public-private partnership or a concessionaire contract is encouraged to consult with and take advantage of the expertise of the facilitator as the government entity determines:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-306(3)(a): whether to enter into the public-private partnership or the concessionaire contract; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-13-306(3)(b): the best way to structure the public-private partnership or the concessionaire contract.


Utah Code Annotated - Title 63N - Chapter 16 - Utah Office of Regulatory Relief
*******************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-102 Definitions.
---------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-102(1): 63N-16-104 "Advisory committee" means the General Regulatory Sandbox Program Advisory Committee created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-102(2): "Applicable agency" means a department or agency of the state that by law regulates a business activity and persons engaged in such business activity, including the issuance of licenses or other types of authorization, which the office determines would otherwise regulate a sandbox participant.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-102(3): "Applicant" means a person that applies to participate in the regulatory sandbox.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-102(4): "Blockchain technology" means the use of a digital database containing records of financial transactions, which can be simultaneously used and shared within a decentralized, publicly accessible network and can record transactions between two parties in a verifiable and permanent way.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-102(5): "Consumer" means a person that purchases or otherwise enters into a transaction or agreement to receive an offering pursuant to a demonstration by a sandbox participant.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-102(6): "Demonstrate" or "demonstration" means to temporarily provide an offering in accordance with the provisions of the regulatory sandbox program described in this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-102(7): 63N-16-103 "Director" means the director of the Utah Office of Regulatory Relief created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-102(8): "Executive director" means the executive director of the Governor's Office of Economic Opportunity.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-102(9): "Financial product or service" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-102(9)(a): a financial product or financial service that requires state licensure or registration; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-102(9)(b): a financial product, financial service, or banking business that includes a business model, delivery mechanism, offering of deposit accounts, or element that may require a license or other authorization to act as a financial institution, enterprise, or other entity that is regulated by Title 7, Financial Institutions Act, or other related provisions.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-102(10): "Health, safety, and financial well-being" includes protecting against physical injury, property damage, or financial harm.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-102(11): "Innovation" means the use or incorporation of a new or existing idea, a new or emerging technology, or a new use of existing technology, including blockchain technology, to address a problem, provide a benefit, or otherwise offer a product, production method, or service.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-102(12): "Insurance product or service" means an insurance product or insurance service that requires state licensure, registration, or other authorization as regulated by Title 31A, Insurance Code, including an insurance product or insurance service that includes a business model, delivery mechanism, or element that requires a license, registration, or other authorization to do an insurance business, act as an insurance producer or consultant, or engage in insurance adjusting as regulated by Title 31A, Insurance Code.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-102(13): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-102(13)(a): "Offering" means a product, production method, or service, including a financial product or service or an insurance product or service, that includes an innovation.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-102(13)(b): "Offering" does not include a product, production method, or service that is governed by Title 61, Chapter 1, Utah Uniform Securities Act.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-102(14): "Product" means a commercially distributed good that is:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-102(14)(a): tangible personal property;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-102(14)(b): the result of a production process; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-102(14)(c): passed through the distribution channel before consumption.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-102(15): "Production" means the method or process of creating or obtaining a good, which may include assembling, breeding, capturing, collecting, extracting, fabricating, farming, fishing, gathering, growing, harvesting, hunting, manufacturing, mining, processing, raising, or trapping a good.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-102(16): 63N-16-103 "Regulatory relief office" means the Utah Office of Regulatory Relief created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-102(17): 63N-16-201 "Regulatory sandbox" means the General Regulatory Sandbox Program created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-102(18): "Sandbox participant" means a person whose application to participate in the regulatory sandbox is approved in accordance with the provisions of this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-102(19): "Service" means any commercial activity, duty, or labor performed for another person.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-103 Creation of regulatory relief office and appointment of director -- Responsibilities of regulatory relief office.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-103(1): There is created within the Governor's Office of Economic Opportunity the Utah Office of Regulatory Relief.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-103(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-103(2)(a): The regulatory relief office shall be administered by a director.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-103(2)(b): The director shall report to the executive director or the executive director's designee and may appoint staff subject to the approval of the executive director.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-103(3): The regulatory relief office shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-103(3)(a): administer the provisions of this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-103(3)(b): administer the regulatory sandbox program; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-103(3)(c): act as a liaison between private businesses and applicable agencies to identify state laws or regulations that could potentially be waived or suspended under the regulatory sandbox program, or amended.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-103(4): The regulatory relief office may:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-103(4)(a): propose potential reciprocity agreements between states that use or are proposing to use similar programs to the regulatory sandbox; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-103(4)(b): in accordance with Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act, and the provisions of this chapter, make rules regarding:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-103(4)(b)(i): administering the regulatory sandbox, including making rules regarding the application process and the reporting requirements of sandbox participants; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-103(4)(b)(ii): cooperating and consulting with other agencies in the state that administer sandbox programs.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-104 Creation and duties of advisory committee.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-104(1): There is created the General Regulatory Sandbox Program Advisory Committee.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-104(2): The advisory committee shall have 9 members as follows:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-104(2)(a): four members appointed by the director who represent business interests and are selected from a variety of industry clusters;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-104(2)(b): three members appointed by the director who represent state agencies that regulate businesses;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-104(2)(c): one member of the Senate, appointed by the president of the Senate; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-104(2)(d): one member of the House of Representatives, appointed by the speaker of the House of Representatives.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-104(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-104(3)(a): Subject to Subsection (3)(b), members of the advisory committee who are not legislators shall be appointed to a four-year term.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-104(3)(b): Notwithstanding the requirements of Subsection (3)(a), the director may adjust the length of terms of appointments and reappointments to the advisory committee so that approximately half of the advisory committee is appointed every two years.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-104(4): (2) Notwithstanding the requirements in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-104(5): A majority of the advisory committee constitutes a quorum for the purpose of conducting advisory committee business, and the action of the majority of a quorum constitutes the action of the advisory committee.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-104(6): 63N-16-105 The advisory committee shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-104(6)(a): advise and make recommendations to the regulatory relief office as described in this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-104(6)(b): 63N-16-105 designate the laws and regulations of an industry for potential study by the regulatory relief office as described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-104(6)(c): annually select a chair of the advisory committee.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-104(7): The regulatory relief office shall provide administrative staff support for the advisory committee.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-104(8): 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107; 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107; 36-2-2
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-104(8)(a): 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107; 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107 A member may not receive compensation or benefits for the member's service, but a member appointed under Subsection (2)(a) may receive per diem and travel expenses in accordance with:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-104(8)(a)(i): 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107 Sections

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-104(8)(b): 36-2-2 Compensation and expenses of a member who is a legislator are governed by Section


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-105 Annual report.
-----------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-105(1): On or before October 1 of each year, the regulatory relief office shall prepare and submit an annual written report to the governor, the Business and Labor Interim Committee, and the Economic Development and Workforce Services Interim Committee for the preceding fiscal year.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-105(2): 63N-16-201; 63N-16-302 The annual report described in Subsection (1) shall include:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-105(2)(a): 63N-16-201 information regarding each participant in the regulatory sandbox created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-105(2)(b): recommendations regarding any laws or regulations that should be permanently modified;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-105(2)(c): information regarding outcomes for consumers;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-105(2)(d): recommendations for changes to the regulatory sandbox program or other duties of the regulatory relief office; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-105(2)(e): 63N-16-302 the information described in Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201 General Regulatory Sandbox Program -- Application requirements.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(1): There is created in the regulatory relief office the General Regulatory Sandbox Program.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(2): In administering the regulatory sandbox, the regulatory relief office:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(2)(a): shall consult with each applicable agency;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(2)(b): shall establish a program to enable a person to obtain legal protections and limited access to the market in the state to demonstrate an offering without obtaining a license or other authorization that might otherwise be required;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(2)(c): may enter into agreements with or adopt the best practices of corresponding federal regulatory agencies or other states that are administering similar programs; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(2)(d): may consult with businesses in the state about existing or potential proposals for the regulatory sandbox.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(3)(a): An applicant for the regulatory sandbox may contact the regulatory relief office to request a consultation regarding the regulatory sandbox before submitting an application.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(3)(b): The regulatory relief office shall provide relevant information regarding the regulatory sandbox program.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(3)(c): The regulatory relief office may provide assistance to an applicant in preparing an application for submission.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(4): An applicant for the regulatory sandbox shall provide to the regulatory relief office an application in a form prescribed by the regulatory relief office that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(4)(a): confirms the applicant is subject to the jurisdiction of the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(4)(b): confirms the applicant has established a physical or virtual location in the state, from which the demonstration of an offering will be developed and performed and where all required records, documents, and data will be maintained;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(4)(c): contains relevant personal and contact information for the applicant, including legal names, addresses, telephone numbers, email addresses, website addresses, and other information required by the regulatory relief office;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(4)(d): discloses criminal convictions of the applicant or other participating personnel, if any;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(4)(e): contains a description of the offering to be demonstrated, including statements regarding:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(4)(e)(i): how the offering is subject to licensing, legal prohibition, or other authorization requirements outside of the regulatory sandbox;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(4)(e)(ii): each law or regulation, accompanied by their statutory reference or citation, that the applicant seeks to have waived or suspended while participating in the regulatory sandbox program;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(4)(e)(iii): how the offering would benefit consumers;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(4)(e)(iv): how the offering is different from other offerings available in the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(4)(e)(v): any identifiable, likely, and significant harm to the health, safety, or financial well-being of consumers that each law or regulation described in Subsection (4)(e)(ii) protects against;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(4)(e)(vi): what risks might exist for consumers who use or purchase the offering;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(4)(e)(vii): how participating in the regulatory sandbox would enable a successful demonstration of the offering;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(4)(e)(viii): a description of the proposed demonstration plan, including estimated time periods for beginning and ending the demonstration;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(4)(e)(ix): recognition that the applicant will be subject to all laws and regulations pertaining to the applicant's offering after conclusion of the demonstration; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(4)(e)(x): how the applicant will end the demonstration and protect consumers if the demonstration fails;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(4)(f): lists each government agency, if any, that the applicant knows regulates the applicant's business; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(4)(g): provides any other required information as determined by the regulatory relief office.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(5): 63J-1-504 The regulatory relief office may collect an application fee from an applicant that is set in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(6): An applicant shall file a separate application for each offering that the applicant wishes to demonstrate.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(7): 63G-2-305 After an application is filed, the regulatory relief office shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(7)(a): 63G-2-305 classify, as a protected record, any part of the application that the office determines is nonpublic, confidential information that if disclosed would result in actual economic harm to the applicant in accordance with Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(7)(b): consult with each applicable government agency that regulates the applicant's business regarding whether more information is needed from the applicant; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(7)(c): seek additional information from the applicant that the regulatory relief office determines is necessary.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(8): No later than five business days after the day on which a complete application is received by the regulatory relief office, the regulatory relief office shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(8)(a): review the application and refer the application to each applicable government agency that regulates the applicant's business;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(8)(b): provide to the applicant:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(8)(b)(i): an acknowledgment of receipt of the application; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(8)(b)(ii): the identity and contact information of each regulatory agency to which the application has been referred for review; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(8)(c): provide public notice, on the office's website and through other appropriate means, of each law or regulation that the office is considering to suspend or waive under the application.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(9): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(9)(a): Subject to Subsections (9)(c) and (9)(g), no later than 30 days after the day on which an applicable agency receives a complete application for review, the applicable agency shall provide a written report to the director of the applicable agency's findings.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(9)(b): The report shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(9)(b)(i): describe any identifiable, likely, and significant harm to the health, safety, or financial well-being of consumers that the relevant law or regulation protects against; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(9)(b)(ii): make a recommendation to the regulatory relief office that the applicant either be admitted or denied entrance into the regulatory sandbox.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(9)(c): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(9)(c)(i): The applicable agency may request an additional five business days to deliver the written report by providing notice to the director, which request shall automatically be granted.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(9)(c)(ii): The applicable agency may only request one extension per application.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(9)(d): If the applicable agency recommends an applicant under this section be denied entrance into the regulatory sandbox, the written report shall include a description of the reasons for the recommendation, including why a temporary waiver or suspension of the relevant laws or regulations would potentially significantly harm the health, safety, or financial well-being of consumers or the public and the likelihood of such harm occurring.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(9)(e): If the agency determines that the consumer's or public's health, safety, and financial well-being can be protected through less restrictive means than the existing relevant laws or regulations, then the applicable agency shall provide a recommendation of how that can be achieved.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(9)(f): If an applicable agency fails to deliver a written report as described in this Subsection (9), the director shall assume that the applicable agency does not object to the temporary waiver or suspension of the relevant laws or regulations for an applicant seeking to participate in the regulatory sandbox.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(9)(g): Notwithstanding any other provision of this section, an applicable agency may by written notice to the regulatory relief office:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(9)(g)(i): within the 30 days after the day on which the applicable agency receives a complete application for review, or within 35 days if an extension has been requested by the applicable agency, reject an application if the applicable agency determines, in the applicable agency's discretion, that the applicant's offering fails to comply with standards or specifications:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(9)(g)(i)(A): required by federal law or regulation; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(9)(g)(i)(B): previously approved for use by a federal agency; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(9)(g)(ii): reject an application that is preliminarily approved by the regulatory relief office, if the applicable agency:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(9)(g)(ii)(A): recommended rejection of the application in accordance with Subsection (9)(d) in the agency's written report; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(9)(g)(ii)(B): provides in the written notice under this Subsection (9)(g), a description of the applicable agency's reasons why approval of the application would create a substantial risk of harm to the health, safety, or financial well-being of the public, or create unreasonable expenses for taxpayers in the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(9)(h): If an applicable agency rejects an application under Subsection (9)(g), the regulatory relief office may not approve the application.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(9)(h)(i): If the applicable agency rejects an application under Subsection (9)(g), the applicable agency shall provide the rejection on a form created by the agency and signed by the director of the applicable agency.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(9)(h)(ii): The form shall document the reason for the rejection and show every reasonable effort was made to meet with the applicant.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(10): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(10)(a): Upon receiving a written report described in Subsection (9), the director shall provide the application and the written report to the advisory committee.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(10)(b): The director may call the advisory committee to meet as needed, but not less than once per quarter if applications are available for review.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(10)(c): After receiving and reviewing the application and each written report, the advisory committee shall provide to the director the advisory committee's recommendation as to whether or not the applicant should be admitted as a sandbox participant under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(10)(d): As part of the advisory committee's review of each written report, the advisory committee shall use the criteria required for an applicable agency as described in Subsection (9).
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(11): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(11)(a): In reviewing an application and each applicable agency's written report, the regulatory relief office shall consult with each applicable agency before admitting an applicant into the regulatory sandbox.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(11)(b): The consultation with each applicable agency may include seeking information about whether:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(11)(b)(i): the applicable agency has previously issued a license or other authorization to the applicant; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(11)(b)(ii): the applicable agency has previously investigated, sanctioned, or pursued legal action against the applicant.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(12): In reviewing an application under this section, the regulatory relief office and each applicable agency shall consider whether a competitor to the applicant is or has been a sandbox participant and, if so, weigh that as a factor in favor of allowing the applicant to also become a sandbox participant.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(13): In reviewing an application under this section, the regulatory relief office shall consider whether:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(13)(a): the applicant's plan will adequately protect consumers from potential harm identified by an applicable agency in the applicable agency's written report;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(13)(b): the risk of harm to consumers is outweighed by the potential benefits to consumers from the applicant's participation in the regulatory sandbox; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(13)(c): certain state laws or regulations that regulate an offering should not be waived or suspended even if the applicant is approved as a sandbox participant, including applicable antifraud or disclosure provisions.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(14): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(14)(a): An applicant becomes a sandbox participant if the regulatory relief office approves the application for the regulatory sandbox and the regulatory relief office enters into a written agreement with the applicant describing the specific laws and regulations that are waived or suspended as part of participation in the regulatory sandbox.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(14)(b): Notwithstanding any other provision of this chapter, the regulatory relief office may not enter into a written agreement with an applicant and related parties that waives or suspends a tax, fee, or charge that is administered by the State Tax Commission or that is described in Title 59, Revenue and Taxation.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(15): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(15)(a): The director may deny at the director's sole discretion any application submitted under this section for any reason, including if the director determines that the preponderance of evidence demonstrates that suspending or waiving enforcement of a law or regulation would cause a significant risk of harm to consumers or residents of the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(15)(b): If the director denies an application submitted under this section, the regulatory relief office shall provide to the applicant a written description of the reasons for not allowing the applicant to be a sandbox participant.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(15)(c): The denial of an application submitted under this section is not subject to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(15)(c)(i): agency or judicial review; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(15)(c)(ii): the provisions of Title 63G, Chapter 4, Administrative Procedures Act.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(16): The director shall deny an application for participation in the regulatory sandbox described by this section if the applicant or any person who seeks to participate with the applicant in demonstrating an offering has been convicted, entered a plea of nolo contendere, or entered a plea of guilty or nolo contendere held in abeyance, for any crime involving significant theft, fraud, or dishonesty if the crime bears a significant relationship to the applicant's or other participant's ability to safely and competently participate in the regulatory sandbox program.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(17): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(17)(a): When an applicant is approved for participation in the regulatory sandbox, the director shall provide public notice of the approval on the office's website and through other appropriate means.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(17)(b): The public notice described in Subsection (17)(a) shall state:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(17)(b)(i): the name of the sandbox participant;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(17)(b)(ii): the industries the sandbox participant represents; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(17)(b)(iii): each law or regulation that is suspended or waived for the sandbox participant as allowed by the regulatory sandbox.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(18): In addition to the information described in Subsection (17), the office shall make the following information available on the office's website and through other appropriate means:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(18)(a): documentation regarding the office's determination and grounds for approving each sandbox participant; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-201(18)(b): public notice regarding any sandbox participant's revocation to participate in the regulatory sandbox.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-202 Scope of the regulatory sandbox.
-----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-202(1): If the regulatory relief office approves an application under this part, the sandbox participant has 12 months after the day on which the application was approved to demonstrate the offering described in the sandbox participant's application.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-202(2): An offering that is demonstrated within the regulatory sandbox is subject to the following:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-202(2)(a): each consumer shall be a resident of the state; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-202(2)(b): no law or regulation may be waived or suspended if waiving or suspending the law or regulation would prevent a consumer from seeking restitution in the event that the consumer is harmed.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-202(3): This part does not restrict a sandbox participant who holds a license or other authorization in another jurisdiction from acting in accordance with that license or other authorization.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-202(4): A sandbox participant is deemed to possess an appropriate license or other authorization under the laws of the state for the purposes of any provision of federal law requiring licensure or other authorization by the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-202(5): (6); 63N-16-201(14); 63N-16-201(14); 63N-16-201(14) Subject to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-202(5)(a): 63N-16-201(14) during the demonstration period, a sandbox participant is not subject to the enforcement of state laws or regulations identified in the written agreement between the regulatory relief office and the sandbox participant described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-202(5)(b): 63N-16-201(14) a prosecutor may not file or pursue charges pertaining to a law or regulation identified in the written agreement between the regulatory relief office and the sandbox participant described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-202(5)(c): 63N-16-201(14) a state agency may not file or pursue any punitive action against a sandbox participant, including a fine or license suspension or revocation, for the violation of a law or regulation that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-202(5)(c)(i): 63N-16-201(14) is identified as being waived or suspended in the written agreement between the regulatory relief office and the sandbox participant described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-202(5)(c)(ii): occurs during the demonstration period.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-202(6): Notwithstanding any other provision of this part:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-202(6)(a): a sandbox participant does not have immunity related to any criminal offense committed during the sandbox participant's participation in the regulatory sandbox; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-202(6)(b): a sandbox participant that provides an offering that is a financial product or service shall comply with all applicable federal laws and regulations governing consumer protection.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-202(7): By written notice, the regulatory relief office may end a sandbox participant's participation in the regulatory sandbox at any time and for any reason, including if the director determines that a sandbox participant is not operating in good faith to bring an offering to market.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-202(8): The regulatory relief office and the regulatory relief office's employees are not liable for any business losses or the recouping of application expenses or other expenses related to the regulatory sandbox, including for:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-202(8)(a): denying an applicant's application to participate in the regulatory sandbox for any reason; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-202(8)(b): ending a sandbox participant's participation in the regulatory sandbox at any time and for any reason.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-203 Consumer protection for regulatory sandbox.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-203(1): Before demonstrating an offering to a consumer, a sandbox participant shall disclose the following to the consumer:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-203(1)(a): the name and contact information of the sandbox participant;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-203(1)(b): that the offering is authorized pursuant to the regulatory sandbox and, if applicable, that the sandbox participant does not have a license or other authorization to provide an offering under state laws that regulate offerings outside of the regulatory sandbox;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-203(1)(c): that the offering is undergoing testing and may not function as intended and may expose the consumer to certain risks as identified by the applicable agency's written report;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-203(1)(d): that the provider of the offering is not immune from civil liability for any losses or damages caused by the offering;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-203(1)(e): that the provider of the offering is not immune from criminal prosecution for violations of state law or regulations that are not suspended or waived as allowed by the regulatory sandbox;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-203(1)(f): that the offering is a temporary demonstration that may be discontinued at the end of the demonstration period;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-203(1)(g): the expected end date of the demonstration period; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-203(1)(h): that a consumer may contact the regulatory relief office and file a complaint regarding the offering being demonstrated and provide the regulatory relief office's telephone number and website address where a complaint may be filed.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-203(2): (1) The disclosures required by Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-203(3): The regulatory relief office may require that a sandbox participant make additional disclosures to a consumer.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-204 Requirements for exiting regulatory sandbox.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-204(1): 63N-16-205 At least 30 days before the end of the 12-month regulatory sandbox demonstration period, a sandbox participant shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-204(1)(a): notify the regulatory relief office that the sandbox participant will exit the regulatory sandbox and discontinue the sandbox participant's demonstration after the day on which the 12-month demonstration period ends; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-204(1)(b): 63N-16-205 seek an extension in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-204(2): (3); (1) Subject to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-204(3): If a demonstration includes an offering that requires ongoing duties, the sandbox participant may continue to do so but will be subject to enforcement of the laws or regulations that were waived or suspended as part of the regulatory sandbox.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-205 Extensions.
--------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-205(1): Not later than 30 days before the end of the 12-month regulatory sandbox demonstration period, a sandbox participant may request an extension of the regulatory sandbox demonstration period.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-205(2): The regulatory relief office shall grant or deny a request for an extension in accordance with Subsection (1) by the end of the 12-month regulatory sandbox testing period.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-205(3): The regulatory relief office may grant an extension in accordance with this section for not more than 12 months after the end of the initial regulatory sandbox demonstration period.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-206 Record keeping and reporting requirements.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-206(1): A sandbox participant shall retain records, documents, and data produced in the ordinary course of business regarding an offering demonstrated in the regulatory sandbox.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-206(2): If a sandbox participant ceases to provide an offering before the end of a demonstration period, the sandbox participant shall notify the regulatory relief office and each applicable agency and report on actions taken by the sandbox participant to ensure consumers have not been harmed as a result.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-206(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-206(3)(a): The regulatory relief office shall establish quarterly reporting requirements for a sandbox participant, including information about any consumer complaints.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-206(3)(b): No later than 14 days after the day on which a sandbox participant submits the sandbox participant's second quarterly report to the regulatory relief office, the regulatory relief office shall provide the sandbox participant's first and second quarterly reports to each applicable agency.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-206(3)(c): No later than 30 days after the day on which an applicable agency receives the reports as described in Subsection (3)(b), the applicable agency shall provide a written report to the regulatory relief office on the demonstration that describes any statutory or regulatory reform the applicable agency recommends as a result of the demonstration.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-206(4): The regulatory relief office may request records, documents, and data from a sandbox participant and, upon the regulatory relief office's request, the sandbox participant shall make such records, documents, and data available for inspection by the regulatory relief office.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-206(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-206(5)(a): The sandbox participant shall notify the regulatory relief office and each applicable agency of any incidents that result in harm to the health, safety, or financial well-being of a consumer.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-206(5)(b): If a sandbox participant fails to notify the regulatory relief office and each applicable agency of any incidents as described in Subsection (5)(a), or the regulatory relief office or an applicable agency has evidence that significant harm to a consumer has occurred, the regulatory relief office may immediately remove the sandbox participant from the regulatory sandbox.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-206(6): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-206(6)(a): No later than 30 days after the day on which a sandbox participant exits the regulatory sandbox, the sandbox participant shall submit a written report to the regulatory relief office and each applicable agency describing an overview of the sandbox participant's demonstration, including any:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-206(6)(a)(i): incidents of harm to consumers;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-206(6)(a)(ii): legal action filed against the participant as a result of the participant's demonstration; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-206(6)(a)(iii): complaints filed with an applicable agency as a result of the participant's demonstration.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-206(6)(b): No later than 30 days after the day on which an applicable agency receives a written report from a sandbox participant as described in Subsection (6)(a), the applicable agency shall provide a written report to the regulatory relief office on the demonstration that describes any statutory or regulatory reform the applicable agency recommends as a result of the demonstration.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-206(7): The regulatory relief office may remove a sandbox participant from the regulatory sandbox at any time if the regulatory relief office determines that a sandbox participant has engaged in, is engaging in, or is about to engage in any practice or transaction that is in violation of this chapter or that constitutes a violation of a law or regulation for which suspension or waiver has not been granted.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-301 Regulatory relief web page.
------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-301(1): The regulatory relief office shall create and maintain on GOEO's website a web page that invites residents and businesses in the state to make suggestions regarding laws and regulations that could be modified or eliminated to reduce the regulatory burden of residents and businesses in the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-301(2): On at least a quarterly basis, the regulatory relief office shall compile the results of suggestions from the web page and provide a written report to the governor, the Business and Labor Interim Committee, and the Economic Development and Workforce Services Interim Committee that describes the most common suggestions.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-301(3): In creating the report described in Subsection (2), the regulatory relief office and the advisory committee:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-301(3)(a): shall ensure that private information of residents and businesses that make suggestions on the web page is not made public; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-301(3)(b): may evaluate the suggestions and provide analysis and suggestions regarding which state laws and regulations could be modified or eliminated to reduce the regulatory burden of residents and businesses in the state while still protecting consumers.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-302 Proactive regulatory relief efforts.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-302(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-302(1)(a): "Regulatory framework" means a framework for determining the risk level to the public if a law or regulation that inhibits the creation or success of new and existing companies or industries were to be permanently removed or temporarily waived.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-302(1)(b): "Risk level" means a level of risk categorized from low, medium, and high.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-302(2): The regulatory relief office may:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-302(2)(a): review, at any time, any existing state laws or regulations that may unnecessarily inhibit the creation or success of companies or industries other than the occupational regulations of individuals reviewed by the Office of Professional Licensure Review under Title 13, Chapter 1b, Office of Professional Licensure Review; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-302(2)(b): provide recommendations to the governor and the Legislature on modifying those state laws and regulations described in Subsection (2)(a).
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-302(3): 63N-1a-202 The regulatory relief office shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-302(3)(a): create a regulatory framework; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-302(3)(b): 63N-1a-202 annually study the laws and regulations of at least two industries selected from:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-302(3)(b)(i): 63N-1a-202 an industry targeted for economic development by the Unified Economic Opportunity Commission as described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-302(3)(b)(ii): an industry designated by the General Regulatory Sandbox Program Advisory Committee for study by the regulatory relief office.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-302(4): In undertaking the review described in Subsection (3), the regulatory relief office shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-302(4)(a): identify any law or regulation that the regulatory relief office determines inhibits the creation or success of new and existing companies or industries;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-302(4)(b): apply the regulatory framework to the identified law or regulation; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-302(4)(c): consider:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-302(4)(c)(i): the history of the identified regulation or law, including the reasons why the regulation or law was originally enacted;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-302(4)(c)(ii): whether the identified regulation or law:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-302(4)(c)(ii)(A): creates an unnecessary barrier to industry for businesses; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-302(4)(c)(ii)(B): imposes an unnecessary cost to businesses or consumers;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-302(4)(c)(iii): whether the penalty for violation of the regulation or law, if any, is proportional to the potential harm; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-302(4)(c)(iv): if there are potentially less burdensome alternatives to the existing regulation or law and apply the regulatory framework to that alternative.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-302(5): 63N-16-105 The regulatory relief office shall submit as part of the report described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-302(5)(a): a detailed overview of the regulatory relief office's study of the laws and regulations as described in this section, including the reasons why the laws and regulations of a particular industry were selected for study and the strategy the office implemented to study the laws and regulations of that industry; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-302(5)(b): recommended changes to a law or regulation identified by the regulatory relief office in Subsection (4) that the regulatory relief office determines:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-302(5)(b)(i): is inhibiting the success of businesses, companies, or industries; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-302(5)(b)(ii): would not present a high risk level to the public if the law or regulation were permanently removed or temporarily waived.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-401 Definitions.
---------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-401(1): "Blockchain company" means an entity that uses blockchain technology to facilitate financial transactions between users.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-401(2): "Noncustodial blockchain company" means a blockchain company that does not have possession or control of a user's private key.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-401(3): 13-62-101 "Private key" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-401(4): 63N-16-402 "Registry" means the Noncustodial Blockchain Registry described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-401(5): "User" means a person who engages in a financial transaction through a blockchain company.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-402 Noncustodial Blockchain Registry -- Contents -- Rulemaking.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-402(1): The regulatory relief office shall maintain a Noncustodial Blockchain Registry that lists noncustodial blockchain companies conducting business in the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-402(2): For each registered noncustodial blockchain company, the regulatory relief office shall include on the registry:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-402(2)(a): the name of the noncustodial blockchain company; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-402(2)(b): the noncustodial blockchain company's authorized agents in the state, if any.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-16-402(3): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act The regulatory relief office may make rules in accordance with

Utah Code Annotated - Title 63N - Chapter 17 - Utah Broadband Center and Access Act
***********************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-102 Definitions.
---------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-102(1): 63N-17-201 "Broadband center" means the Utah Broadband Center created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-102(2): "Final proposal" means the submission provided by the state to the Assistant Secretary of Commerce for Communications and Information as part of the state's BEAD Application, as set forth in 47 U.S.C. Sec. 1702(e)(4).
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-102(3): "Initial proposal" means the submission provided by the state to the Assistant Secretary of Commerce for Communications and Information as part of the state's BEAD Application, as set forth in 47 U.S.C. Sec. 1702(e)(3).
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-102(4): "Letter of intent" means the submission provided by the state to the Assistant Secretary of Commerce for Communications and Information as part of the state's BEAD Application, as set forth in 47 U.S.C. Sec. 1702(e)(1)(B).
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-102(5): "Public-private partnership" means an arrangement or agreement between a government entity and one or more private persons to fund and provide for a public need through the development or operation of a public project in which the private person or persons share with the government entity the responsibility or risk of developing, owning, maintaining, financing, or operating the project.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-102(6): 63N-17-301; 63N-17-401 "Subgrantee" means an entity that receives funds from the state under:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-102(6)(a): 63N-17-301 the Broadband Access Grant Program created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-102(6)(b): 63N-17-401 the Broadband Equity Access and Deployment Grant Program created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-102(7): "State BEAD application" means a submission by the state for a grant under the federal Broadband Equity Access and Deployment Program established under 47 U.S.C. Sec. 1702(b), consisting of a letter of intent, initial proposal, and final proposal.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-201 Utah Broadband Center -- Creation -- Director -- Duties.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-201(1): There is created within the office the Utah Broadband Center.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-201(2): The executive director shall appoint a director of the broadband center to oversee the operations of the broadband center.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-201(3): 63N-17-203; 63N-17-202 The broadband center shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-201(3)(a): ensure that publicly funded broadband projects continue to be publicly accessible and provide a public benefit;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-201(3)(b): 63N-17-203 develop the statewide digital connectivity plan described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-201(3)(c): 63N-17-202 carry out the duties described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-201(3)(d): administer the Broadband Access Grant Program in accordance with Part 3, Broadband Access Grant Program; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-201(3)(e): administer the Broadband Equity Access and Deployment Grant Program in accordance with Part 4, Broadband Equity Access and Deployment Program.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-201(3)(f): The broadband center shall ensure efficiency with respect to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-201(3)(f)(i): expenditure of funds; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-201(3)(f)(ii): avoiding duplication of efforts.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-201(3)(g): The broadband center shall consider administering broadband infrastructure funds in a manner that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-201(3)(g)(i): efficiently maximizes the leverage of federal funding;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-201(3)(g)(ii): avoids the use of public funds for broadband facilities that duplicate existing broadband facilities that already meet or exceed federal standards; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-201(3)(g)(iii): accounts for the benefits and costs to the state of existing facilities, equipment, and services of public and private broadband providers.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-202 Infrastructure and broadband coordination.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-202(1): 63A-16-505; 63N-2-206 The broadband center shall partner with the Utah Geospatial Resource Center created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-202(1)(a): voluntarily submitted broadband availability, speeds, and other broadband data;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-202(1)(b): voluntarily submitted public utility data;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-202(1)(c): 63N-2-206 workforce data, including information regarding:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-202(1)(c)(i): 63N-2-206 enterprise zones designated under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-202(1)(c)(ii): public institutions of higher education; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-202(1)(c)(iii): APEX accelerators;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-202(1)(d): transportation data, which may include information regarding railway routes, commuter rail routes, airport locations, and major highways;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-202(1)(e): lifestyle data, which may include information regarding state parks, national parks and monuments, United States Forest Service boundaries, ski areas, golf courses, and hospitals; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-202(1)(f): other relevant economic development data as determined by the office, including data provided by partner organizations.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-202(2): The broadband center may:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-202(2)(a): make recommendations to state and federal agencies, local governments, the governor, and the Legislature regarding policies and initiatives that promote the development of broadband-related infrastructure in the state and help implement those policies and initiatives;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-202(2)(b): facilitate coordination between broadband providers and public and private entities;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-202(2)(c): collect and analyze data on broadband availability and usage in the state, including Internet speed, capacity, the number of unique visitors, and the availability of broadband infrastructure throughout the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-202(2)(d): create a voluntary broadband alliance, which shall include broadband providers and other public and private stakeholders, to solicit input on broadband-related policy guidance, best practices, and adoption strategies;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-202(2)(e): work with broadband providers, state and local governments, and other public and private stakeholders to facilitate and encourage the expansion and maintenance of broadband infrastructure throughout the state; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-202(2)(f): in accordance with the requirements of Title 63J, Chapter 5, Federal Funds Procedures Act, and in accordance with federal requirements:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-202(2)(f)(i): apply for federal grants;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-202(2)(f)(ii): participate in federal programs; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-202(2)(f)(iii): administer federally funded broadband-related programs.

---------------------------------------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-203(2): "Strategic plan" means the statewide digital connectivity plan created in accordance with Subsections (2) and (3).

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-203(4)(d): apply for additional funds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-203(5): In developing the strategic plan, the broadband center shall work with the commission.

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-203(6)(a): implementation of the commission's recommendations;

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-203(6)(d): strategic plan implementation;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-203(6)(e): grants received in addition to those described in Subsection (6)(b);
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-203(6)(f): projects funded in addition to those described in Subsection (6)(b); and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-203(6)(g): recommendations for legislation.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-203(7): The broadband center shall submit the strategic plan to the commission for the commission's recommendation before finalizing the strategic plan.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-203(8): On or before October 1 of each year, the broadband center shall report to the commission and the Public Utilities, Energy, and Technology Interim Committee regarding status updates.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-301 Creation of Broadband Access Grant Program.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-301(1): As used in this part:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-301(1)(a): "Eligible applicant" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-301(1)(a)(i): a telecommunications provider or an Internet service provider;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-301(1)(a)(ii): a local government entity and one or more private entities, collectively, who are parties to a public-private partnership established for the purpose of expanding affordable broadband access in the state; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-301(1)(a)(iii): a tribal government.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-301(1)(b): "Underserved area" means an area of the state that is underserved in terms of the area's access to broadband service, as further defined by rule made by the broadband center.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-301(1)(c): "Unserved area" means an area of the state that is unserved in terms of the area's access to broadband service, as further defined by rule made by the broadband center.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-301(2): There is established a grant program known as the Broadband Access Grant Program that is administered by the broadband center in accordance with this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-301(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-301(3)(a): The broadband center may award a grant under this part to an eligible applicant that submits to the broadband center an application that includes a proposed project to extend broadband service to individuals and businesses in an unserved area or an underserved area by providing last-mile connections to end users.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-301(3)(b): Subsection (3)(a) does not prohibit the broadband center from awarding a grant for a proposed project that also includes middle-mile elements that are necessary for the last-mile connections.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-301(4): In awarding grants under this part, the broadband center shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-301(4)(a): based on the following criteria and in the order provided, prioritize proposed projects:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-301(4)(a)(i): located in unserved areas;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-301(4)(a)(ii): located in underserved areas;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-301(4)(a)(iii): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-301(4)(a)(iii)(A): that the eligible applicant developed after meaningful engagement with the impacted community to identify the community's needs and innovative means of providing a public benefit that addresses the community's needs; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-301(4)(a)(iii)(B): that include, as a component of the proposed project, a long-term public benefit to the impacted community developed in response to the eligible applicant's engagement with the community;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-301(4)(a)(iv): located in an economically distressed area of the state, as measured by indices of unemployment, poverty, or population loss;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-301(4)(a)(v): that make the greatest investment in last-mile connections;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-301(4)(a)(vi): that provide higher speed broadband access to end users; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-301(4)(a)(vii): for which the eligible applicant provides at least 25% of the money needed for the proposed project, with higher priority to proposed projects for which the eligible applicant provides a greater percentage of the money needed for the proposed project; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-301(4)(b): consider the impact of available funding for the proposed project from other sources, including money from matching federal grant programs.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-301(5): For a project that the eligible applicant cannot complete in a single fiscal year, the broadband center may distribute grant proceeds for the project over the course of the project's construction.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-301(6): In awarding a grant under this part, the broadband center shall ensure that grant funds are not used by a subgrantee in a manner that causes competition among projects that are substantially supported by state funds or federal funds subgranted by the state, as determine in accordance with rules made by the broadband center in accordance with Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-301(7): 63G-2-305 As provided in and subject to the requirements of Title 63G, Chapter 2, Government Records Access and Management Act, a record submitted to the broadband center that contains a trade secret or confidential commercial information described in Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-302 Duties of the broadband center.
----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-302(1): (1)(a); (c) The broadband center shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-302(1)(a): establish an application process by which an eligible applicant may apply for a grant under this part, which application shall include:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-302(1)(a)(i): a declaration, signed under penalty of perjury, that the application is complete, true, and correct; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-302(1)(a)(ii): an acknowledgment that the eligible applicant is subject to audit;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-17-302(1)(b): establish a method for the broadband center to determine which eligible applicants qualify to receive a grant;

Utah Code Annotated - Title 63N - Chapter 18 - Utah Center for Immigration and Integration
******************************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 63N-18-102 Definitions.
---------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 63N-18-102(1): 63N-18-201 "Center" means the Utah Center for Immigration and Integration created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-18-102(2): "Foreign labor" means one or more individuals from a nation other than the United States who are eligible to participate in visa programs established by the federal government to work in the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-18-102(3): "Foreign labor program" means a program established by the United States Department of Labor to bring eligible foreign individuals to the United States for employment opportunities.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-18-102(4): "Immigrant integration" means a dynamic two-way process in which immigrant communities and host communities work together to build a cohesive and vibrant society that has respect for unique cultural differences.


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-18-201 Creation of the Utah Center for Immigration and Integration -- Responsibilities of the center.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-18-201(1): There is created within the Governor's Office of Economic Opportunity the Utah Center for Immigration and Integration.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-18-201(2): The center shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-18-201(2)(a): assist individuals and businesses in the state with identifying pathways for recruiting and retaining foreign labor;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-18-201(2)(b): coordinate with state agencies in developing and administering policies and programs related to immigrant integration;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-18-201(2)(c): develop and implement a statewide strategy for immigrant integration that promotes economic opportunities for immigrant communities in the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-18-201(2)(d): create and convene a task force to review and make recommendations regarding the state's policies on immigrant integration;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-18-201(2)(e): develop sustainable partnerships with local officials, the business sector, and community organizations serving immigrant communities in the state; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-18-201(2)(f): advise and make recommendations to the governor, state agencies, and the Legislature regarding immigrant integration and foreign labor issues.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-18-201(3): The center may not encourage a business to bypass state residents for the business's workforce needs.
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-18-201(4): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act The center may, in accordance with


Utah Code Annotated § 63N-18-202 Annual report.
-----------------------------------------------
The office shall include in the annual written report described in SectionUtah Code Annotated § 63N-18-202(1): a description of the center's activities regarding immigrant integration;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-18-202(2): the number of businesses that received assistance in utilizing foreign labor programs;
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-18-202(3): the number of employment-based immigration visas issued for individuals to secure employment opportunities in the state, including the primary employers associated with the visas; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-18-202(4): 63N-18-201(2)(d) recommendations regarding:
Utah Code Annotated § 63N-18-202(4)(a): changes that would improve the center; and
